when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她的確是做一些事 , 但真正的事情是 , 真正的意思是 , 未來將會遠遠超過這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這傢伙出現了 , alanturing , 在1936年 , 然後又發明了一台電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全理論化了 ,
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都從數學的觀點出發 , 但turing告訴我們一些非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他奠定了數學在電腦科學上的基礎 , 說: 「 你怎麼把電腦創造出來的並不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	你的電腦是不是像babbage那樣是純機械的 , 或是像現在的電腦一樣是不重要也許未來是細胞 , 或是再說一次是機械的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米技術
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器只要把它做得很小 , 所有的東西都是電腦
there is in a sense a computing essence .	在某種意義上是有計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做 「 教堂 」 的論點 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	所以 , 突然間 , 你就有了這個連結 , 你說巴貝奇打造的這個東西就是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們現今用電腦做的所有事 , 只有很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓各位了解有多慢 , 有一個1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它用打孔卡 , 原本被放進去的 , 跑得比第一台zx81要慢一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個ram背包
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要 , 可以加入許多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	那麼 , 我們今天在哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在windon科學博物館的檔案中有上百個計劃和上千頁文獻是charlesbabbage寫的關於這個分析引擎
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一組計畫 , 我們稱之為計劃28 , 這也是我與doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的計算機負責人 , 也是負責打造出不同引擎的人 , 我們的計劃就是打造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有許多部分可以用 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其一是掃描babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這是已經完成的 。 第二個是對所有計劃的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是一個模擬那機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部份是到科博物館去建造它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它被建造時 , 你終於能夠了解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為你面前的不是小小的晶片 , 而是看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作的聲響 。 我說不定還聞的到 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫到 , 一旦分析引擎的存在 , 它一定會引導未來的科學 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有打造過它 , 因為他總是在拓展新計劃 , 但當它真的在1940年代被建造出來時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我先讓各位稍微了解一下它的動作狀況 , 影片上只顯示cpu運作的機械原理之一 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪它準備做加法 。 這是加法的運作原理所以你想像這個巨大的機器
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年時間
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代以前 , 我們將有
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這場以影像呈現的演講中 , 雅恩•亞伯特蘭展示了他三項最近的一項人類活動 , 我們的棲息地在他的一系列 「 從天而降 」 影像中展示了他的星球上所拍攝的照片 , 他個人在世界各地的訪談節目《六十億人》中所拍攝的電影 , 他很快就推出了《家》 , 這部影片中記載了人類對於環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變化、環境、電影、未來、人道、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannarhusbertrand從廣角度捕捉到脆弱的地球
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球造成很大的影響 , 可以搭飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我排放了 , 在大氣中 , 九噸二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態 , 一年內我以一個法國人的身分 , 排放出的二氧化碳量相當於一個法國人 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我該怎麼辦呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我回家時還得殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我得要用另一種方式來抵消我的碳 , 就像我每次都做一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是呈現出我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我會給你們看一些例子 , 關於我去年所拍攝的最後一張照片 。

coral reef in new caledonia .	新喀里多尼亞的珊瑚礁

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在這場tedxboston的無障礙演說中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克說明了便宜且快速的基因定序是如何將健康照護顛倒過來 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療、科學、科技、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	richardresnick:歡迎來到基因革命
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	女士們先生們 , 我為大家介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方是性別染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男性有x染色體 , 當然 , 還有y染色體的小複製品 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	很抱歉男孩們 , 但這只是一個小東西 , 讓你不一樣 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以如果你放大這個基因組的圖片 , 會看到雙螺旋結構生命的編碼是由這四個生化字母組成 , 或者我們稱之為基對 , 對吧:a、c、g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組有多少基因組 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以隨便亂丟大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但 , 事實上 , 如果我把這1280年的每一個像素上一個基對放在800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3000塊螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的是相當大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	或許是因為有一群人順便一提 , 有y染色體的人決定想要定序它 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	所以 , 15年 , 事實上 , 還有約40億美元之後 , 基因組序列並發表了 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後的版本發表了 , 他們繼續努力 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在一個類似這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每根鹼基的成本大約一美元-很慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們將一組基因做了50份複製 , 將全部的複製品分割成50基對 , 然後我們將它們排序 , 大量平行排列 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後把這些帶入軟體中 , 重新組合 , 告訴你們故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給大家看看這是什麼樣子的 , 人類基因組計畫:3gb , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	每週可以做2000億基對 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天 , 600年的變化將達到600年 , 這速度的減慢並沒有任何跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 要定序一個基對 , 一個基對的價格已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這就相當於你1998年給汽車加滿一次油的錢 , 一直等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星又開回來兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口 , 電腦普及 , 所有醫學文獻的檔案 , 摩爾定律 , 舊方法的定序 , 而這就是所有的新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數尺度 , 你通常不會看到線向上 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	所以全世界用在人類基因組測序的能力可以在今年做到5萬到10萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	而我們基於被放置的機器而知道這個現象 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	在可預見的未來裏每年這個數目會變成兩倍、三倍甚至四倍
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一間實驗室佔據了總容量的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	中國人絕對可以在新的月球上打贏這個比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有何意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人年紀是37歲
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她提出了 「 階段二 」 雌激素受阻體陽性乳癌
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術 , 化療和放射性治療
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後她又發現了第三個卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她42歲又回來了 , 帶著更多的卵巢癌 , 化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又患上了急性骨髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 8天後就會死亡 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	所以 , 首先 , 小至10年 , 這位女性接受的待遇 , 會像放血方式一樣 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	正是因為我的同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學基因組研究所的同事rickwilson決定要研究一下這位女性的事務
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他依序排序 , 用了皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚 , 以及有癌骨髓的骨髓 , 將兩者的基因組排序幾週後 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	接著 , 他在軟體中比較了這兩組基因 , 他發現 , 在30億個鹼基中 , 有兩千個鹼基缺損 , 一個叫做tp53的基因 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因上有這種具有殺傷力的突變基因 , 你一生中有百分之九十的可能性會患上癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這對這位女性並沒有任何幫助 , 但如果你願意 , 就會造成很嚴重、很深刻的影響 , 會影響到她的家庭 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我是說 , 如果他們有相同的突變基因檢測 , 並且獲得相同的基因檢測 , 然後他們可以去定期接受檢查 , 並且可以及早發現癌症 , 並且有可能更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我為各位介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出大腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信這些症狀並不搭配 , 透過一些英勇的努力 , 和許多網際網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫界 , 事實上 , 他們還有別的 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們有的就是多巴反應性肌張力不全的肌張力不全症
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	他們得到了左旋多巴 , 症狀的確有所改善 , 但卻不是完全符合症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	原來這張照片的這位先生是一位叫joebeery的先生 , 他很幸運是一家叫做生命科技的公司的首席執行長 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是製造大量全基因組測序工具的兩家公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是讓他的孩子接受定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現 , 在一個叫做spr的基因上有一系列突變 , 這其中有一種叫做spr的基因 , 負責製造血清素 , 和其他的基因 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以 , 在左旋多巴的基礎上 , 他們給這些孩子使用了血清素前的藥物 , 現在他們非常正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有全基因組測序是不可能發生的 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	而在幾年前--這要花費10萬美金--
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	現在只要1萬美金 , 下一年就有1千美金
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	就在它變成100元以後 , 送出或花一年的時間
that's how fast this is moving .	移動得如此之快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這是小小的尼克•喜歡蝙蝠俠和水槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 肚子嚴重落下 , 就像饑荒的受害者一樣 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他進食時 , 他的腸道基本上打開了 , 排泄物溢出到他的腸子中 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	於是數百次手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 , 我現在好多痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的兒童科醫師恰巧有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他完全不知道發生了什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓我們把這個孩子的基因組定序吧 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	而他們發現的是在一個控制細胞死亡的基因上有一處單點變異
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以這理論是說 , 他對食物的本質產生了一些免疫反應 , 那是很自然的反應 , 導致一些被編譯出來的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但管制這樣的基因是失靈的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	所以 , 這也說明了 , 當然 , 其中一種治療骨髓移植的方法 , 是他做骨髓移植的 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的緊縮康復後 , 他現在正用a1醬汁在吃牛排了 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	使用基因組作為普遍診斷的前景今日就在我們身邊了 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 這裡

which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你能想到地球上人類的足跡 , 以及我們有能力維持食物產量的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來製造新一行的玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 以及其他對乾旱、洪水、害蟲和農藥有高度包容力的農作物 。

consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	基因組學的消費者應用會蓬勃發展 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫展示了他的骨髓採取器一個新裝置 , 它很快就收集了能拯救生命的骨髓 , 帶到捐贈者的最小痛苦 。 他強調骨髓中所發現的成體幹細胞可以用來治療許多臨終疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。
