so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是史丹佛大學的小兒科癌醫師及幹細胞研究員我的臨床研究重心是骨髓移植
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	我受到去年ted講者jillboltetaylor的啟發 , 沒有帶上人類的大腦 , 但我帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓 , 其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 他們大部分患有較高級的惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤和其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前我在史丹佛移植獎學金
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 還有bob , 她是志願捐贈者
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們要把他的骨髓發送到全國 , 拯救兒童白血病的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這塊骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個完整的o.r.團隊、麻醉醫師、護士 , 還有另一個醫生在我面前 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob躺在桌上 , 然後我們將這種小針 , 你知道 , 不要太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的方法是把這個針筒放在軟組織裡 , 每次用針筒將它打入硬骨頭 , 通往tuchus的名詞 , 每次用針筒取出大約十毫升骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把它交給護士 。 她將它注入到一個錫罐 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	再交回給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地這麼做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	到最後 , 我的手臂酸痛 , 我手上有這麼一個呼喚 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的屁股尾端看起來就像這個 , 像瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這樣的流程四十年來並沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	應該有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了一種微創的方法 , 一種我們稱為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新儀器 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而 「 骨髓採取器 」 , 它的運作方式如下:
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準來看待病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	相對於進入骨骼幾十次 , 我們只需要輸入一次 , 到臀部的前面或後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個有彈性、有動力的導管 , 有一個特別的電線圈圈 , 它停留在堅固的骨髓裡 , 遵循臀部的輪廓 , 當它四處移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它讓你可以很快的冒出熱情 , 或吸出豐富的骨髓 , 很快地穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過同一個入口多次 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	因此 , 非常快的 , bob只需一個刺穿 , 局部麻醉 , 並將之作為門診病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛得到了一個小補助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	再玩一下這個 。
and our team members developed this technology .	而我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們又拿到兩隻大型動物 , 以及豬研究
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令人驚訝的是 , 我們不僅僅得到了骨髓 , 而且我們從骨髓採取的骨髓細胞活性 , 比起正常的裝置 , 還得到了十倍的幹細胞 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置去年剛被美國食品藥物管理局批准
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是一名活體病人 。 你可以在有彈性的曲線附近看到 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	這邊會有兩條路過 , 在同一個病人 , 來自同一個洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在局部麻醉、門診以門診做出來的 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	比起標準的方法 , 同一個病人 , 我們的幹細胞 , 大約多了三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	那你為什麼要在乎呢 ? 骨髓是成體幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	它們潛力無窮 , 但還未進入臨床試驗階段 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們全身 , 包括我們骨髓內的血液組織 , 這種細胞形式長達四十年來一直在使用 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年 , 有爆炸性的骨髓幹細胞 , 用以治療病患其他的疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、骨科用藥、組織工程 , 甚至是神經系統用以治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛公佈 , 正在商業化今年2.0世代 「 骨髓採取器 」
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望可以取出更多幹細胞 , 轉化為更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	它可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你在年輕時還能去銀行自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 用在未來你應該需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這張照片是我們的骨髓移植倖存者 , 他們每年都會在史丹佛聚會聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來能有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garretlisi提出了一個爭議性的宇宙模型 , 這個模型可能可以解答所有重大問題 。 如果沒有其他東西的話 , 它是最漂亮的 「 基本粒子 」 和 「 原子力 」 的8維模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技、
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	嘉瑞特.萊西對他的理論的一切理論
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看這些致命的方程式吧 !
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 在接下來的十八分鐘裡我會盡力在不用方程式的前提之下描述粒子物理的美好
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明我們可以從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗和不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一個珊瑚的頭上都有成千上萬的珊瑚群 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會不斷地繁殖和分枝 , 成為基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這會是高智商的珊瑚 , 我們就能讓一個人脫身 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他到底是怎麼走到這個特定的地點 , 跟他的鄰居比起來 , 如果是剛好是命運 , 或是命運 , 又是什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	現在 , 在我們被告知要把溫度調高過頭之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題非常愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以很有意義 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的疤痕 , 可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這一池水會持續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居是和他一模一樣的複製品 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他所有地點 , 但身為獨立的個體 , 體驗到不同的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支長成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 高智商的珊瑚可以獨一無二地準備了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學非常準確地描述了我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是持續分成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 把思想包裹起來是一件很奇怪的事 , 畢竟我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪性 , 最初是由薛丁格和他的貓提出的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓比較喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這組裝中 , 薛丁格待在一個有放射物質的箱子中 , 根據量子力學定律 , 量子力學的分支被分成了放射狀狀態 , 一個不受輻射照射的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本輻射擴散的分支中 , 它會啟動一個觸發點 , 釋放毒氣 , 薛丁格已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支中 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些現實是分開的 , 每一個個體都有的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	就兩種情況來說 , 另一種都不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很怪 , 因為我們每一個人都只經歷一個個體的存在 , 而我們看不到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格 , 是種不同可能性的珊瑚分支 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是微小世界的運作方式
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都可以做
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不代表每件事都發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理學的其他部分則用來描述哪些可以發生哪些不可以
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都可用幾何學歸根結底以及基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動是完全平衡的情況下才能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我將講說明我們對這些粒子的認識它們是什麼以及這個平衡是如何運作的
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中 , 一束質子和反質子被加速到接近光速的速度然後相撞產生出一股單純的能量爆炸
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這些能量會立刻轉換成亞原子的噴霧現象 , 有了偵測器和電腦 , 用來找出它們的屬性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這部機器是日內瓦的大型強子對撞機周長有17英里運轉時耗電是蒙特雷市的五倍
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法確切地預測哪些粒子會在每一次的碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有的可能性都已經實現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們什麼是粒子可以產生的 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量一定跟質子和反質子的能量一樣多 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量極限更大的粒子都不會產生 , 且對我們來說仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新型粒子加速器那麼令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越過去7倍的能量極限 , 因此我們很快就會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談論我們可能看見的事物之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	亞原子的一整個動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	現場很多人都過得很好的生活 , 把他們推到一旁
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有中和的夥伴 , 叫做中子 , 沒有電荷和質量 ,
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上下夸克有很大的質量 , 三者相結合 , 使原子內的質子和中子結合 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	這些粒子分為兩類左旋和右旋它們都有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有我們不太熟悉的第二代和第三代同樣的載荷和第一代相同但質量更高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子會和各種力量產生交互作用
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	帶電粒子通過光子傳遞電磁力相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力 , 叫做微弱的力 , 只與左撇子的物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間強力的作用力帶有一種不同的載荷叫做色荷 , 並且有三種不同品種紅、綠、藍
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪默里•蓋爾曼這些名字都是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後是重力 , 它的質量和物質相互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都對應有不同的載荷
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種力通過各自粒子所攜帶的載荷和物質發生作用
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見但我們很確定存在的粒子就是希格斯粒子它給予所有其他粒子的質量
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是看到希格斯粒子我們確信它會成真
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的奧秘在於我們還能看到什麼
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示這場演講的結尾美麗的可能性
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的自旋和載荷計算所有不同的粒子共有226種
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	要追蹤這些粒子的數量很多 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子 , 似乎很奇怪
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們按他們各自的載荷把他們畫出來有些美麗的圖案出現了
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子擁有一個負電荷而夸克擁有1/3的電荷
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合成一個質子時 , 它會有總電荷加一加一 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 它們的載荷相反 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	現在 , 電荷實際上是另兩種載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間上畫出粒子的載荷電荷就在這些粒子的垂直方向上
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這種模式
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	稱為電弱統一模型於1967年組裝
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以只熟悉電荷 , 是因為希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子質量很大破壞了電弱型式的對稱性
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	通過給弱子較大的質量使弱力更加弱
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯粒子沿著水平方向分佈在這張圖中 , 電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量 , 在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力在二維空間中被這種粒子載荷的型式所描述
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力沿兩個載荷的方向表示出來然後將載荷用夸克形式沿這些方向畫出來
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中畫出來然後投射到二度空間以便我們能看到它們
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	無論粒子相互作用自然會在這四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和它的反粒子相撞會產生能量四個電荷方向的載荷總量為零
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以產生只要有相同的能量並保持總載量為零
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如說這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須保持平衡 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子而這三個的總載荷仍然是零
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持一個完美的平衡
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不僅漂亮
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	告訴我們什麼樣的互動是允許的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 以便更好地看出強相互作用 , 這個交互作用有著很好的六角形對稱 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中強子像是這個會和有色夸克相互作用比如這個綠夸克會給夸克帶來不同顏色的夸克
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	而強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每一個原子裏發生上百萬次使原子核保持一體
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但對應到三股力量的這四種載荷還不是故事的結局 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以納入兩個載荷相對應的重力力量 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	包括這些 , 每個粒子都有兩種不同的自旋載荷 , 自旋和自旋 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中形成了一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看看它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這模式符合我們目前對於大自然如何以微小的粒子規模建造出的最佳知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們能確定的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗中能達到的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道了這些微小尺度的粒子物理 。 宇宙與這些小尺度一起運作的方式 , 是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談談關於我們還不知道的事的新古老觀念 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能否取得整個enchilada的雙手 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們希望找到構成我們宇宙的所有粒子和力量
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖片來預測新的粒子 , 也就是當實驗達到更高能量時 , 我們會看到的粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有個古老的想法 , 這種已知的載荷圖案 , 不太對稱 , 可以從更完美的圖案中浮現 , 有點類似希格斯粒子如何突破電弱圖案以產生電磁感 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引入具有新載荷方向的新力量 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們導入一個新方向時 , 我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子帶有什麼樣的載荷 , 然後再讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜測明智的話 , 我們可以在六度載荷空間中構建標準載荷集 , 作為更完美的七度載荷空間圖案的對稱組成 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這個選擇與1973年由pati和salam推出的一個大統一理論相應 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的合成圖案 , 我們可以看到一些缺口 , 在那裡粒子似乎不見了 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的研究方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家會尋找更大、更對稱的模式 , 把已定的模式納入為子集的結構 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的圖案讓我們得以預測那些從未見過的粒子的存在
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 作用力應該和弱力很相似 , 只是比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這個載荷集並且想想這個關於物質粒子的奇怪事實:在六度載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代物質擁有和第一代物質擁有完全相同的載荷
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子通過對應的六個載荷無法特殊的識別
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間上彼此相互坐著
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以賦予每一個粒子獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整體的圖案是什麼樣的 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代用一種叫 " 三重性 " 的對稱性和第一代相關
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案 , 其實是數學中最漂亮的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	李群是光滑曲線形的248維空間
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案的每一點都對應到這個複雜而美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的彎曲時空
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	再加上量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以描述宇宙怎麼用最小的尺度運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	八度載荷空間中這個形狀的圖案是非常美麗的 , 它可以概括成千上萬種這種基本粒子間的相互作用 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的表面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它 , 我們可以看到包含其中的許多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過特定的旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿著對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是非常美麗的物體 , 如同其他統一理論一樣 , 我們可以看到一些孔洞 , 在這裡 , 新的粒子是這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	在這有20個空格需要新粒子其中兩個已有帕蒂和薩拉姆粒子填補
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案的位置我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣稀少的原子但具有色荷且和強力相互作用
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子使圖案完整讓我們得到完整的e8
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著很深的數學根基 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	許多人認為它是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這是一個了不起的前景一個偉大數學美麗的天體可以用可想像的最小尺度描述粒子相互作用的真相
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	大自然被數學所描述的這個想法一點也不新 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年伽利略寫下這句話: 「 大自然的偉大著作 , 即停止對我們的凝視 , 以數學的語言寫的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他的幾何形狀 , 沒有了這些 , 根本不可能理解其中的任何字 ; 如果沒有這些 , 就有一個在黑暗的迷宮中遊走 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的我也試過按照伽利略的指導只用三角形圓形和其他幾何形狀來描述粒子物理的數學性
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家實際在研究這東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但可以確保在這個數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學一起形成的數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個正在成長的e8珊瑚同時粒子在每個可能的位置相互作用著一個美麗的圖案
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	隨著圖案的使用像是大型強子對撞機這樣的新機器時 , 我們也許能知道大自然是如何使用e8圖案還是不同的圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個探索過程是一個奇妙的探險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那就非常非常酷
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新粒子但不符合這個圖案那會非常有趣但對e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然也對我個人不利
now how bad would that be ?	那到底有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 還不錯 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然的運作是個很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論及其它類似的理論都是長拍 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部份這些想法可能最後都不會是大自然的真理 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有大量的毀滅
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	這樣看來新物理理論和新創公司很像 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同對任何大型投資 , 當它還沒成功時 , 在情感上很難放棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有東西沒有用 , 你就得要丟掉它 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	在這種不確定中 , 唯一能夠保持理智並獲得幸福的方法就是在人生中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡我所能去過一個平衡生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理愛情和衝浪中尋找平衡我三個載荷的方向
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 就算我研究的物理學也沒有實現 , 我仍然知道我已經過著美好的生活 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	並試著生活在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是我父母最大的謎團之一 , 我如何能在這樣的時刻活下來 , 而不去面對全職工作 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島辦公室裡的景色 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到這些美麗的景象類似 , 但在稍微不同的位置 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一個很不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我把時間花在喜歡做的事情上
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	流浪的生活方式有時很辛苦 , 但卻讓我能生活在美麗的地方 , 並保持我人生中所能享有的平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚相處 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也非常享受超級聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能被邀請到ted來 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我可能明白其中的百分之二 , 但我還是很喜歡 。 所以我會聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論我很習慣珊瑚
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:是的 。 能讓少數人興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它能把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說我們應該想到宇宙 , 它的核心是最微小的東西 , 存在的可能性是否為e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我是說 , 有沒有一個量表可以達到最小的程度 ? 或嗎 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:現在我展示給你們看的模式與我們所知的基本粒子物理原理相應這已經是一個很漂亮的形狀了
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這就是我說的那個我們知道是肯定的
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	那個形狀和e8有著明顯的相似處 , 可能是其他的圖片 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點狀圖案 , 實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 它們在我們所體驗到的空間中 , 會被扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了所有我們看到的基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但弦理論家 , 就我所理解的 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待e8的電子 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	高爾:不 , 它會是這個e8形狀對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它會扭曲 。 當它移動的時候它會扭曲的方向就是我們看到的粒子 。 所以 , 它會是...克:e8形狀的大小 , 電子的大小 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	大一點嗎 ? 小一點嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	高爾:就我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這會是最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以在量子場論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是 , 所有的可能性都同時在擴展和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這也是為什麼我用比喻來形容珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的進入方式將會是一個連接時空中每一點的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	正如我所說的形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時它的扭曲方向就是基本粒子本身
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	所以 , 透過量子場理論 , 他們表現出自己的形象是點 , 並且以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能講得更清楚
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它激起了一種驚奇感 , 我當然想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常感謝你們的到來 。 這真是太棒了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇的黑猩猩研究者珍古德談到坦尚尼亞還有其它的社區計畫 , 幫助非洲繁榮的小鎮人士肩並肩生活 , 充滿威脅的動物 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學、
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古德幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以這樣說 , 斷奶、橡皮筋、馬鈴薯 , 但是我們也可以ooh、ooh、ooh、ooh、ooh、ooh、oh 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所發出的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從這一群巢穴傳到下一處 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	今天晚上 , 我想接下我要演講的內容 , 來自昨天的zeray所留下來的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇的三歲南猿小孩塞拉姆
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽到了基因圖譜中人類的歷史、家族樹、人類的歷史、基因圖譜 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	是一位古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯利基 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩之路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在當時是相當非比尋常的 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在的確頗為普遍 , 但他的論點是因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石知道很多生物的樣子從肌肉連接的形狀來判斷它們是如何從各式各樣的文物中判斷出生物的樣貌
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然行為並不是化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張-現在已經是個很常見的理論 , 如果我們發現一些行為模式相似或相同於我們現存最接近的遠親--人猿 , 以及今天的人類 , 也許這些行為是在七百萬年前出現在人猿類型的人類祖先身上 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把那些特質從古老的歷史中帶過來
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看一下現今針對人類進化論所做的教科書 , 你經常會發現人們依據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比任何其他生物更像我們 。 我們在這次的ted會議中也聽到了很多 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 對我來說 , 黑猩猩和人類一樣的方式 , 還是對某些特定面向的行為作出評論 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有牠或牠自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給牠們取名字 。 牠們可以活到六十歲或更久雖然我們認為大部份的牠們在野外不會活到六十歲
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	溫柔先生 。 母蚊子在11至12歲時生了第一個小孩 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那之後 , 她每五到六年就有一個嬰兒 , 很長的童年依賴期 , 當那個孩子在照顧的時候 , 晚上和母親一起睡 , 和她的背一起騎 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的孩童期對黑猩猩很重要 , 就像對我們來說 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物進化時越來越複雜 , 所以我們發現 , 在個體的人生歷史中 , 學習扮演著越來越重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿牠們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 透過這種方式 , 現已在非洲各個黑猩猩族群中看到不同的使用工具的方式 , 這些行為如何從一個世代的傳承到下一個世代 , 通過觀察、模仿和練習 , 如此一來 , 我們就可以把這些使用工具的行為描述成是原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口說的語言 。 我們剛剛已經談過了
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們的確擁有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 當中有許多都很相似 , 甚至與我們的一模一樣 , 以同樣的情境形成 。 迎接黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們還會親吻、握手、拍另一個人的背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	然後他們會大搖大擺地往下丟石頭 ,
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現許多、很多的例子都是同情心、由愛出發的 , 以及真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 就像我們人類一樣 , 牠們也有天生的黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	它們具有極端殘暴的能力 , 甚至一種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常積極的行為 , 大部分來說 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的對象 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們是十分具侵略性的 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩們 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經讓我們瞭解 , 畢竟人類和其它動物界之間並沒有一條清晰的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這條界線非常的模糊 , 隨著我們做更多的觀察 , 它時常變得更加的模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍在持續進行 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些生活在野外的複雜社會關係中的黑猩猩們 , 比起其他任何事情 , 都來幫助我們意識到我們是其中的一份子 , 而不是單純分割 , 那些與我們共同生活的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 要找到和世界上許多其他生物一樣的黑猩猩 , 還蠻讓人感傷的 , 牠們正在失去棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張由空中拍攝的照片 , 上面顯示了岡貝森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那是我十六年前飛越整片地區時 , 我意識到 , 在公園之外 , 在1960年 , 這個森林尚未被砍伐 , 沿著坦岡易科湖的東岸 , 那裡是一個很小、只有三十平方公里的岡貝國家公園的所在地 , 有一個問題出現在我腦海中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們該如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當生活在國家公園附近的人們正為了生存而苦掙扎時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	住在那裡的人 , 比土地可能還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	持續增加的難民們如洪水般從蒲隆地湧入並從剛果湖邊游過來 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	而非常貧窮的人們他們無法負擔得起從別處購買食物
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱它為坦尚尼亞造林計劃 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	用一種整體的方式來改善在公園附近村莊的人們的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	一開始只有12個村莊 , 現在已經24個村莊了
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間詳細說明 , 但它包含了諸如樹木護理法 , 最適合這種已退化、近似沙漠的土地 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤流失的方法
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度使用的農地 , 讓農地在兩年內能重新生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	為了幫助村民們從井裡獲取淡水 ,
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些校間
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同全世界的情況一般 , 我們有95%的貸款都退還了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦權婦女 , 與教育合作 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 這樣她們才能讀完中學 , 以明確的了解到 , 隨著女性教育的增長 , 全世界的家庭人數減少 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供節育計畫和愛滋病相關的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	這個計畫的結果是 , 有些事發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	對於保育這24個村莊的農夫們 , 沒有把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子 , 順便說一句 , 很多工作人員現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但是當我們開始坦尚尼亞造林計劃時 , 那是一個坦尚尼亞人進入村子 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊與村民對話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對沒有
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的必要性 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白 , 隨著山坡的上層覆蓋許多樹木 , 所以你得到了這片可怕的土壤侵蝕和土石流 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	今天 , 我們正在開發更大的岡貝生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這個區域遠離國家公園 , 延伸到所有這些十分貧瘠的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落擁有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實會同意將百分之十到二十的高地邊緣的土地保留下來 , 所以再一次的 , 當樹木長回來之後 , 黑猩猩們就會長出葉門走廊 , 藉此可以與國家公園外的其他遺傳群體進行互動 。
so tacare is a success .	所以 , 坦尚尼亞造林是個成功 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們把它複製到非洲的其它區域 , 其它荒野面臨極端人口壓力的地方 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們前面這幾天一直在討論的 , 都是很重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有著很大的貧窮
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有許多人居住在並不是那麼肥沃的土地 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木 , 土壤開放土壤 , 造成了流失 , 因為絕望的人口砍伐越來越多的樹木 , 所以他們可以嘗試種植食物給他們自己和家人 , 會發生什麼事 ? 必須要付出代價 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	而其他問題不只在非洲 , 還有其他發展中國家的問題 , 的確 , 無所不在地 , 我們對我們的星球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家 , 愛德華.威爾森說過 , 如果地球上每個人都能維持像歐洲人或美國人一樣的生活水準 , 我們需要三個新的地球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說四個 。 但我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	究竟發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 這裡的問題是 , 我們現在可以說是地球上最聰明的生物 , 擁有非凡的頭腦 , 能夠擁有這麼好看的科技 , 被這些ted研討會展示出來 , 然而我們卻破壞了唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做了重大決定之前 , 曾經坐下來問自己: 「 這個決定如何影響我們未來的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定 , 我在這裡談的不是非洲 , 而是已開發國家的主要決策 , 涉及數百萬美元 , 通常都是基於 「 這會如何影響下次的股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各處旅行時 , 談論黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 以及他們消失的森林 , 我了解到越來越多的非洲問題 , 可以解決以前殖民時代剝削的問題 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 在歐洲演說 , 在美國演說 , 前往亞洲 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	不論到哪裡 , 都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我在說什麼 。 我說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們所呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 ,
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害著我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源可能是我們本世紀所面臨的最關鍵的課題之一 , 到處都是水受到農業、工業和家庭化學品污染 , 這些化學物仍然被世界各地噴灑 , 看似無法從過去的經驗中獲利 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯造成的效應更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤流失 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們不計後果的燃燒化石燃料加上其他溫室氣體 , 所以說 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候出了什麼問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	世界各地的氣候是混雜的 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且更受影響的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	已經受影響的非洲 ,
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱狀況更加糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季來臨時 , 它很常導致洪水加重的苦難 , 以及貧窮、飢餓與疾病的惡性循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	居住在無法支撐的地區的人數 , 窮到無法購買食物的人數 , 他們不能搬離家鄉 , 因為整片土地都被降解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以 , 當最後一棵樹被砍伐時 , 沙漠化 , 令人毛骨悚然 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這樣的事並不只發生在非洲 。 在全世界都是這樣 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我一點也不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時我遇到許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為可以有某種程度上的落差存在於這不尋常的聰明大腦中 , 像ted科技所展示的那樣的 , 和人類的心 ? 用非科學的角度來看待它 , 用愛和同情心來談論它 , 會不會有一些落差 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上他們是憂鬱的 , 或冷漠的 , 或痛苦和憤怒的 。 他們說的或多或少都是一樣的 。 「 我們會這麼想 , 是因為我們覺得你已經損害了我們的未來 , 卻束手無策 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經損害了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每次我看著他們時 , 我就會想 , 從我還是他們那個年紀開始 , 我們是如何傷害這個美麗的星球的 , 我就感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這個計畫就是我們稱為根與芽的計畫 , 這個計畫始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已經散播到全世界97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	具有象徵性的意義 。 根形成堅固的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來很小 ; 為了要到達陽光 , 它們能突破磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆看成是我們在地球上所造成的所有問題 , 環保和社會問題 。 這是關於希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人可以突破這困境 , 為所有生物創造一個更美好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	" 根與芽 " 計畫所傳達最重要的訊息是我們每一個人每天都有所作為
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們是有選擇權的 。 我們每一個人都能選擇我們想要做些什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人別無選擇 , 要靠我們來改變現狀 , 讓窮人也能選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽計畫所有人都要選擇三個計畫 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 和哪個國家 , 不論他們身處城市或鄉村 , 或什麼樣的計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人開始做他們自己的根與芽團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	而每一個小組都能在它們之間做選擇 , 三個不同類型的專案計畫來讓這個世界更美好 , 認知到這些不同的問題彼此間 , 互相影響 , 進而影響彼此 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以他們的其中一個計畫是幫助他們自己的人類社群
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能籌集資金幫助世界其他地區的社區
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物們 , 不只是野生的動物們 , 還有馴養的動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的計畫之一是要幫助我們所共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這一切當中 , 都是一個訊息 , 就是學習去以和平與和諧的方式生活在我們自己、家庭、我們的社區、國家、文化、文化、宗教 , 和我們與自然世界之間 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們現有的速度繼續破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們所擁有的不超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只要挑選其中一個或兩個在非洲的計畫 , 根與芽的團體正在進行 , 一兩項計畫只在坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果 , 獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 正如我所說的 , 目前在全球97個國家進行 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們正在種植樹木 。 他們在種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營中工作 , 和雞在一起 , 以一點點錢賣蛋 , 或只是用它們來養家糊口 , 感受到自豪感和自主權 , 因為他們不再無助且依賴他人 , 只靠他們所種的蔬菜和雞隻 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它在烏干達也被運用在一些心理上的幫助 , 幫助那些前男兵 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	進行這樣子的計畫 , 就是把他們帶離自己 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是社會中有用的一份子 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄中也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有時間更多的根與芽了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要組成部份 , 較年長的孩子和較年輕的孩子說話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而非自願性的懷孕之類的年輕人則傾聽著其他年輕人而非成年人
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望這就是我在世界各地被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你看到了這麼多糟糕的事情 , 你看到你的黑猩猩數量減少了大約一百萬隻的數量 , 在本世紀之初 , 沒有超過十五萬隻的數量 , 和許多其他動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失了 , 曾經是森林的地方沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣沒有希望的大會 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中之一是神奇的人腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想一想技術
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我實在太激動了 , 到了人們談論堆肥式廁所的時候 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的嗜好之一 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水往洗衣機旁邊沖 , 狀況很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	然後談到再生能源極其重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否為我們的孩子關心這個星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩、孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們是否關心他們的未來 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的菁英份子 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以做出選擇 , 來作為我們每天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 , 我們穿什麼
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用這個問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	會如何影響我孩子長大後的人生 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 或其他的 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的大腦 , 與人的心結合 , 我們會與世界各地的手聯手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這也是ted能幫助我們的原因 , google也協助我們 , esri也幫我們在岡貝國家公園繪製地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在我們把它們連結起來 , 它開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你們已經聽過了 , 現在開始
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這個改變 , 這個改變 。 若我們關心未來 , 我們就必須要看到我們必須要有的改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個對希望的理由是令人驚異的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一塊完全被摧毀的區域 , 只要有時間 , 或許再一些幫助 , 就可以再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而坦尚尼亞造林計劃就是一個例子 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴過你 , 看似已死去的樹木殘根 , 如果你停止砍伐木材 , 你就不需要因為你已經有了很多的木材 , 那麼在五年之內 , 你就可以擁有一棵30呎高的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎就在絕種的邊緣 , 可以有第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	它啟發著我 。 它也帶領我找到希望的最後一個範疇 , 而我們在過去兩天內聽到這麼多:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 人類的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 所以那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病擊垮的人們 , 或其他那些可以將他們自己抽離出來的東西 , 有時還能帶著幫助 , 帶著他們在社會中扮演的角色 , 帶著他們改變世界的角色 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	試想一下 , 從非洲出來的一兩個人 , 他們真的是很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出一份很長的清單 , 但顯然尼爾森•曼德拉從17年的辛勤勞工發展出來 , 23年的監禁 , 擁有這驚人的寬恕能力 , 讓他能夠領導他的國家在沒有血腥對抗的情況下擺脫種族隔離的惡劣政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的沙羅維瓦對大型石油公司進行的調查 , 儘管全世界的人們竭盡所能地被處決 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是多麼的鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是我們在非洲年輕人所需要的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境榜樣 , 今天也聽過一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以 , 我很感激這個機會能再次將這個訊息分享給ted的各位 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人可以聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	在那個會議中 , 管理這整場會議的年輕女子最後一個字我今天見到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她拿著證書 , 十分興奮 。 她是根與芽的 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這能協助她做到她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我非常非常興奮 , 能夠見到她 , 並僅僅是其中一個例子 , 當他們被賦予權力時 , 給予他們機會行動 , 讓這個世界變得更好 , 真正是我們明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩分享了一些困難的事實 , 關於塑膠污染在海洋中、在我們的生活中 , 以及一些想法 , 說明如何將我們自己從塑膠垃圾回收中解放 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球性議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:關於塑膠污染的艱難事實 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的發起人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在用塑膠袋 , 我剪裁和縫紉 , 做為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 在過去二十年間 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成兩個和三度空間的碎片 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	大約八年之後 , 我有些作品開始產生裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠碎片 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 ,
it's ephemeral just like us . "	簡直就像我們一樣 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	在對塑膠的教育再進一步教學後 , 我發現這是一件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	把塑膠分解成小塊的壞東西 , 因為它永遠都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	而我們發現在海洋環境裡有很多
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 過去幾年 , 我了解到太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我最初的反應 , 我認為這是很多人第一次對學習這件事情的反應 , 「 天哪 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去把這東西清理乾淨 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的發展出一套提案 , 要搭貨船出海 , 以及兩艘退休的拖網漁船、起重機、一台拖船 , 和一台拖網機 , 以及一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的意圖是要出去垃圾漩渦 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 開始把這些塑膠磨碎 , 放進一點點冰冷的模塊裡 , 以便成為可能在未開發之社區中建造材料的磚塊 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始跟實際去過垃圾漩渦去研究塑膠問題的人談 , 談到實際去清理塑膠的人相對於全世界每天實際上產生的塑膠量 , 我必須退一步 , 探討更大的全景 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	而更大的狀況是:我們需要找到一個可以關掉水龍頭的方法 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要停止使用一次就丟棄的塑膠 , 這些塑膠每天以全球性的規模侵入海域 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以從這點來看 , 我也了解到 , 我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心你在想在太平洋的中間的塑膠 , 我現在知道有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦 , 可能是全球五大洋中五大洋的塑膠垃圾 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我擔心的不只是塑膠垃圾的漩渦還有超市裡塑膠的漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 我所有的食物都被塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都以塑膠包裝 , 即使是在健康食品市場 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裏的塑膠還有從塑膠滲出到我們體內的毒素
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群在研究這個問題的人合作 , 我們成立了 「 塑膠污染聯盟 」 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多計畫在進行 , 但有一些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	其一是:如果我們在海裡發現的垃圾中有80%到90%都是塑膠那為什麼不叫它是塑膠
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	資源回收 , 每個人好像就這樣結束了他們的書籍 , 內容是關於永續、綠化 , 都帶著回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	把一些東西放到垃圾桶裡 , 然後就不用再考慮了 。
what is the reality of that ?	事實是什麽 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收的比例不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細觀察 , 尤其是談到塑膠瓶大部分只能降級回收、焚化 , 或運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被降級回收並作成較低的產品 , 而玻璃瓶又可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 或是再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不可能再次變成塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是一個大問題
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們在看的另一件事是要求人們思考的是我們把第四個環放到 " 減量、再利用、回收 " 的前面 , 用三個r , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	儘管可能的話 , 盡量拒絕使用過即丟的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 ; 有些是很老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我自己現在在收集這些超酷的pyrex容器 , 用它們來取代玻璃和保鮮盒 , 來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要拿起一個不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶都很容易 , 如果你去旅行 , 你已經忘記帶一個不銹鋼瓶裝水 , 或過濾水 , 相對之下 , 購買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在座的各位說些什麼──我知道你們對這個議題了解很多──就是這在海洋中是個很大的問題 , 但這是個我們身為消費者所創造的問題──也就是我們能解決的問題 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以解決這個問題 , 透過喚起大家的意識 , 教導大家選擇一些替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 盡可能地選擇單一使用塑膠的替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這條莖切割成我們的海洋 , 藉此 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這場pattiemaes在麻省理工學院的實驗室做示範 , pranavmytry的演示是ted的雜誌的雜誌 。 這是一個可以穿戴的裝置 , 配上一個投影機 , 為和我們的環境創造深刻的互動 。 想像 「 關鍵報告 」 , 然後 , 一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	示範、設計、界面設計、科技、
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派蒂摩斯和帕納•密特里•第六森特 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很有興趣 , 關於我們能否進化出或發展出第六感 , 一種能夠讓我們幾乎接觸到新陳代謝或現存資料的無縫機會 , 能夠協助我們決定我們要面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	你們有些人可能會認為 , 現今的手機不就已經做到這點嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted與別人會面時-當然這就是最好的網絡網絡紀錄年你不會和某人握手然後說: " 你能等一下嗎我拿出手機然後用google查詢你 ? "
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你到超級市場站在那巨大的廁所衛生紙走道時 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 上一個網站 , 來決定這些不同的衛生紙中哪種購買能力是最環保的 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們無法很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 只能協助我們做出最佳的決定 , 決定接下來要做什麼 , 採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能以一種簡單的方法取得這些資訊 , 且不需要使用者改變他們的任何行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡揭露我們最近的努力 , 目前為止 , 最成功的努力 , 還在持續進行中 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我身上正戴著這個裝置我們把零件用架子上的零件組裝起來順便一提 , 到目前為止只需350美元
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我帶著一台攝影機 , 只是一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一台可攜式、用電池驅動的投影系統 , 只有一點鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些零件傳達了我口袋裡的手機的通訊和運算設備 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生 , 帕納•密絲利 , 他真的是一位天才 , 一直在執行和設計這整個系統 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統如何讓他走到任何平面前 , 開始用他的手與投影在他面前的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤這四隻顯著手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著大家可能認得的簡單標記帽 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本你也可以把指甲塗上不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上能追蹤這四隻手指並且辨識出他做出的任何手勢舉例來說 , 他可以直接去看看一個長灘的地圖 , 放大和縮小等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統還能辨識出具代表性的手勢例如 「 照相 」 手勢 , 然後照張相看你面前的事物 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	然後當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何一面牆前將他拍攝的照片投影出來 , 整理這些照片 , 然後重整它們 , 等等 , 同樣是使用自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	兩年前你們有些人可能也來過這裡看過傑夫•韓所做的示範或許有人會想: 「 這不是很像微軟的表面桌嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也會用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但它的不同點在於你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何平面前 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以取得 , 且和這個投影出來的資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 也可以是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 一個重要的不同點是 , 它完全是移動式的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同點是 , 量產後它的成本不會高於今天的手機 , 而且不會變成一個更大的包裝看起來比我脖子上掛的版本還要時髦的多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除此之外 , 讓你們其中一些人活出那種看起來很酷的 「 關鍵報告 」 裡的湯姆克魯斯的幻想 , 我們之所以對這個裝置感到非常興奮 , 是因為它真的可以扮演這六感裝置中的其中之一 , 它給你有關你面前事物的相關資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以我們看到帕納進入超級市場去買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一樣產品-這個系統可以辨識出他所撿到的產品 , 使用影像辨識或是標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以要求額外的資訊
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 在他的個人標準下 , 這個選擇是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能想拿出最多漂白劑的衛生紙而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以取得亞馬遜書局的評分 。 它會直接投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜得到了很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納轉了這本書的頁面 , 接著就能看到更多關於這本書的資訊 , 關於這本書的讀者留言 , 也許是他最喜歡的評論家所提供的資訊等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到一頁特定的頁面 , 他會找到我們一位朋友的專家所寫的註解 , 給了他一些額外的資訊 , 關於特定頁面的任何資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙時它從來就不需要過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你能看到關於你正在閱讀的事件的影片註解 , 你能得到最新的體育分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這個較具爭議性的
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與別人互動時 , 也許你可以看到一個字雲 , 上面的標籤 , 和那個人相關的字句在他們的部落格及個人網頁上 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機有興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你你的航班延誤 , 登機門已經改變 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	而且 , 如果你需要知道現在是什麼時間 , 那就跟在手臂上畫手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	所以 , 目前我們正在開發第六感 , 讓我們可以取得所有關於我們可能遇到的事的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 像我說的 , 他背後的天才
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到很多掌聲因為我覺得他在過去三個月中沒睡多少次
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友也可能對他不太高興 。
