and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道呢 , 或許再十年後我們會帶著植入腦內的終極第六感來這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	菲菲斯.羅德里格茲和阿克瓦菲有強大的友誼 , 生於無法想像的喪失之際 。 rodriguez的兒子在世界貿易中心於2001年9月11日被殺 ; 埃瓦菲的兒子zacariasmoussaui被定罪於那些攻擊中的角色 , 並且被判處死刑 。 希望找到和平 , 這兩個媽媽在此刻得以了解另一件事 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治議題、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	九一一的療癒母親們發現寬恕 , 友誼
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	菲莉思•羅德里奎茲:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說卻是很自然的 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次知道兒子是在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否在直到36小時後死去 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們很害怕我們的國家將會做些什麼事以我們兒子之名---我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 和我家人--
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 卻受到了驚嚇 , 驚嚇 , 和我們生命中那可怕的爆炸 , 真的就是我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項對恐怖主義的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他判處死刑如果罪名成立的話 , 我和我先生和我公開反對這判決的結果 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過那也透過人權團體 , 我們和其他受害者家屬一起被召集 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控時也走過來 , 我心想: 「 真是一個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 我想見見那位女士時 , 我強壯一點 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍在深深的哀傷之中 ; 我知道我沒有這份力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道總有一天我會找到她 , 或是我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當別人聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我馬上得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子所被指控的事 , 她並沒有得到這樣的同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦就等於我了 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以 , 我們在2002年十一月見面 , 現在aicha會告訴你這一切是怎麼來的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	女士們先生們 , 艾維菲:午安 , 女士們 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織讓我和受害者的父母親聯絡 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭認識 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她
she was the only mother in the group .	她是這群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟姐妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我從她的眼睛裡看到 , 她也是一個母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我遭受很大的痛苦
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 在我十六歲時失去了第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以和zacarias的故事實在是太過份了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然痛苦 , 因為我兒子就像是被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子而哭 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 。 我不知道他是否受到折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這樣我的痛苦是其他女性所帶來的正面影響 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人 , 所有賦予生命的媽媽 , 你可以奉獻 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手一起做些什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性這是為我們 , 為我們女人為我們的孩子
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我講反抗暴力 , 反抗恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年青的穆斯林女孩說話 , 讓他們不接受只在很年輕的時候跟她們結婚 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 避免她們跟我一樣的結婚和受苦 , 嗯 , 這是一些好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是我站在你們面前的原因 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我要說我從aicha身上學到很多東西從我們第一次見面的其他家庭成員---這是一個私人的會議 , 因為那時是2002年11月 , 坦白說 , 我們很害怕那個時候的超級愛國主義--我們這些家庭成員們 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 為什麼她想跟我們見個面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她就緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 我們為什麼想見她呢 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們互相想要什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們認識彼此的名字或其他東西之前 , 我們就已經欣然落淚了 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	接著 , 我們圍成一個圓圈 , 圍著支持、提供協助 , 從人們體驗到這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	然後 , aicha開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無罪 , 但我想告訴你 , 我是如何為你的家人所發生的事感到難過 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道這是怎樣的苦痛 , 我覺得如果犯罪 , 人應該受到公平的審判及懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她就是那樣接觸我們 , 我想說 , 那是個破冰者 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	那時發生的事 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 身為人類 , 我們都連結在一起 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	在那個下午完結的時候--大概是午餐後的三小時--我們就覺得好像我們已經彼此認識了一樣 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 不僅是女人 , 在現今的情況下 , 能夠如此慷慨 , 以及在她兒子身上所做的事 , 和她所經歷的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過一個人有著如此艱苦的人生 , 來自這麼一個完全不同的文化和環境和我的環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我非常重視這一點 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都和害怕他人有關 , 但踏出那一步 , 接著了解到: 「 嘿 , 這並不難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能和誰見面 , 不知道我是誰 , 或我和誰有這麼不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字可以做結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說我們必須試著去認識其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你必須要寬容 , 你的心也必須要寬容 , 你的心念必須要寬容 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定是忍不住的 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有朝一日 , 我們都能以和平共處 , 彼此尊重 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世上太多無法取得乾淨的飲用水了 。 工程師麥可普立查做了點事情 , 發明了可攜式的生命體過濾器 , 它可以在幾秒鐘內得到最多可飲用的水 。 這是2009年tedglobal的驚人示範 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水資源 。
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	麥可普立查德的過濾水變成了飲用水變成了骯髒的飲用水 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談論幾件事情
the first thing is water .	第一件事是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都在享受這會議所提供的水 , 在過去的幾天裡 ,
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得這是來自安全的來源 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果不是這樣呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是從這樣的來源著手呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	統計數字還會說你們之中有一半的人現在都得了痢疾 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談過很多關於統計 , 以及為所有人提供安全的飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但他們似乎無法撐過去 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我已經找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	這是因為 , 用當前的思考 , 問題的規模似乎太大了 , 以致於無法思索解決問題 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就這樣關掉:我們、政府、和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想讓大家以不同的角度去思考問題已經解決 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始演講到現在 , 全球各地又有13 , 000人正在腹瀉患者 。
and four children have just died .	而且四個小孩剛剛死去
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶是因為我生氣了 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大部分人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節的隔天 , 看著電視上不斷報導南亞海嘯摧毀性的新聞 , 上映在電視上 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾天和幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝下被污染的水 , 或面對死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	那令我印象深刻 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	接著 , 幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風往美國衝浪而來 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 ! 」 我心想: 「 這裡第一個世界國家 , 看看他們能做什麼吧 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道這花了五天才把水運到超大穹頂嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相開槍 , 只為了電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時我決定我得要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	現在我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 在接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 還有在我的廚房裡 , 讓我太太很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過幾次失敗的原型後 , 我終於想到這個:lifesaver濾水瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好吧 , 現在來談一下科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver濾水瓶之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌 , 大約200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	那肯定會穿過那些200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lifesaver濾水瓶的孔隙只有15奈米大小 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以沒有什麼能度過的 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好吧 , 我來示範一下
would you like to see that ?	你們想看看嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了不少時間設定這些 , 所以我猜我應該這麼做 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們在美好的牛津城裡
so someone's done that up .	有人已經這樣做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	美好的牛津城 , 我做的是從流過牛津的河水取得一些水 , 而泰晤士河 , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我開始想 , 你知道 , 如果我們身在發生水災的災區孟加拉 , 水不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以我拿了一些東西來加進去 。
and this is from my pond .	這是從我的池塘來的 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞一下吧 , 攝影師先生
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們只需要倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	麥可.普立查:好的 。 我們還有一些從污水處理場流出的工廠 。

the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifesaver濾水瓶的原理其實很簡單
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水掀起來 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個罐子來展示給大家看 。 讓我們用那個小便便 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	那還不夠骯髒 。 讓我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好 , 那我要把這些非常骯髒的水 , 放進這裏來 。 你還想要喝一杯嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好了 。 可以了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些打氣筒 , 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這就是所有必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	現在只要我拉開這個東西 , 無菌的飲用水就會跑出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	我得快點 , 準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	完成了 。 小心電器 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	那是安全、無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	來了克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	什麼是它的味道 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯在節目中其他部分的節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好的 。 世界各地成千上萬的人使用了lifesaver濾水瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	會維持6000公升
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 利用故障安全技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	把馬桶拿出來 , 把一個新的進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	對另外6 , 000公升都好 。
so let's look at the applications .	我們來看看它的應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統的危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	接著 , 幾個星期之後 , 我們成立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到營地取用安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病會傳播 。 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只會變成自我延續 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但只要用不同的方式思考 , 運送這些東西 , 人們就可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 並開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	現在 , 並不需要天然災害才可行 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的思維 , 像是國家基礎建設和管道的工作 , 實在是太貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你用計算機把數字用完 , 你就用光了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這裡是 「 不同想法 」 的部分 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程來實現它 , 讓我們使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費除去水中鹽分 , 運送到那裡 , 倒到山上、河流和溪流中 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 鄰近水源的地方 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的只是將它消毒而已 。 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	嗯 , 我們可以用lifesaver濾水瓶
or we could use one of these .	或者使用這種
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在jerry罐頭上
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這將能夠處理二萬五千公升的水 ; 這足夠一個四歲的家庭 , 三年之久 。
and how much does it cost ?	到底要花多少錢呢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大約只需半分錢 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 在用水的時候就用水處理 , 母親和孩子不用再每天漫步四小時來取得他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的來源取得
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	所以只要八十億美元 , 我們就可以達成千禧目標的目標 , 讓無法取得安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	以情境來看 , 英國政府每年花費約120億英鎊於國際援助 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停下來 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	結果就是每年因此受苦的三十五億人 , 以及每年因死亡的兩百萬名兒童 , 將會活下去 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪•奧許諾聲稱我們正生活在歷史上的一個時刻 , 權力正在以從未有的方式改變 。 在tedxbrussels的一個咒語演講中 , 他提出了他即將看到的三個重大的轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策 , 全球議題 , 政治 , 世界文化 ,
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	帕迪阿什唐:全球權力轉移的現象 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩這麼寫道這是一位很有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	據說在1930年代邱吉爾的腦部迴盪
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這樣寫的: 「 在夏日的idle山 , 躺著 , 流著溪流 , 我聽見遠方的鼓聲 , 像在夢裡的聲音 , 遙遠的、低沉的、高大的 , 在路上迴盪著 , 親愛的 , 親愛的朋友和食物到粉末 , 士兵走路 , 很快就要死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩詞有興趣的人 , 這首詩是 " ashropshire小姐 " 由豪斯曼所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但 , 豪斯曼所知道的 , 也在尼爾森交響曲中也聽到了 , 十九世紀那漫長 , 炎熱 , 遍地林木的夏天穩定不穩定 , 即將來臨時 , 我們正要踏進歷史上一段令人害怕的時期 , 當權力改變時 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	女士們先生們 , 這些都是月經週期伴隨著騷動還有很多時候都是血腥的
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我想傳達的訊息是 , 我相信我們會被譴責 , 如果你願意 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻之一 , 那時所建立的權力正開始改變 , 新的世界觀 , 世界上存在的新勢力正開始成形 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是--而且我們今天很清楚的看到--幾乎總是非常動盪的時代 , 高難度的時代 , 而且往往都是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便說一下 , 這種事每世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會爭辯說 , 上次發生時--那是休士曼所感受到的--也就是 , 邱吉爾也同樣感受到當權力從舊的國家開始 , 歐洲的舊勢力跨越大西洋 , 到美國新興的新興強國時期的強國──那是美國本世紀初 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那個時候歐洲人過時的權力被投入兩場血腥的災難就在那最後一個世紀兩場災難分別是兩次偉大的世界大戰
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經把他們稱為歐洲內戰 , 它可能是更精確地形容他們的方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	嗯 , 各位先生女士 , 我們正處於這樣的時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想要談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	在這之中 , 前兩項是關於權力移轉的
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個主題是關於一個新的面向我想參考它從來沒有像現在這樣發生過
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談權力轉移到世界的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	而今天發生的事 , 在某種意義上 , 很可怕 , 因為這從來沒發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們看到了希臘權力的橫向移轉到羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明時發生的權力移轉 。 但我們看到的有些微的不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不只是國與國之間的橫向移轉 ,
it's also moving vertically .	也有直向移轉
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今所發生的權力 , 受到責任的牽制也受到法律的牽制現在國家的機構已開始大量地移入全球的舞台
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力雖然我們說是全球化市場但事實上卻是全球化權力
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層級裡權力是被責任歸屬於法律的層級在國際舞台上則否
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台也是現在存在權力的全球舞台:互聯網的力量、衛星廣播的力量、貨幣改變的力量 。 這個巨大貨幣的力量 , 循環了32倍的流動貨幣交易所必要的金錢數量是過去財政變動者的32倍 , 比起金融投機更有錢的力量 , 使我們都聚集在近期 , 促成了大型企業發展的預算計畫 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球化的空間 , 幾乎沒有受到法律規範的限制 , 人們可能就此行動 , 不再受限制 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	那適合當前強大的力量 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	這總是適用於那些擁有最強大力量的人 , 不受約束 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 不受管制的法律規範 , 不只限於你想要的國際貿易 , 網路 , 等等 。 還有一些你不希望的國際犯罪 , 國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911的揭示是即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 那些空間依然可以攻擊你的人 , 即使在九月的一個早晨 , 都可以攻擊你 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 四百萬美元中的六成被拿去資助911恐怖攻擊的錢 , 其實是通過雙子星大樓的機構911摧毀 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	你看 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播的空間 , 來繞過他們的毒藥 , 這關乎破壞我們的系統和方法 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早 , 無論如何 , 歷史的規則是權力決定權力的管理必須遵守 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 如我所相信的 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代的挑戰之一就是把統治者帶上國際舞台 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在我們面前的幾十年將會是一場更大或更小的亂流 , 或多或少是我們能夠達成的目標:將統治者帶上國際舞台 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要設立一些全球民主制度
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 我自己的看法是 , 女士們先生們 , 這不太可能發生 , 因為他們推出了更多的聯合國機構 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 就必須發明
the world needs an international forum .	這個世界需要的是一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個手段 , 讓你能將國際行動合理化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但談到全球空間的管理 , 我猜這不會發生 , 透過建立更多聯合國的機構 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	實際上 , 這會發生在有力人士聚集在一起 , 形成以條約為基礎的系統、以條約為基礎的協議 , 來統治這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你仔細看 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:合約為底的組織 , 完全以合約為基礎 , 然而 , 強大到足以支撐最強大的國家 , 美國 , 如果有必要的話 , 就要考慮到 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:努力想創立一個合約為底的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在我們知道我們必須組一個能夠把統治權帶到那個金融空間的機構為了財務上的猜想
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是二十國集團因而建立的 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題了 , 我們等下會再回到這裡 , 如果你把最有權力的人聚集在一起 , 訂定了條約性的制度 , 來填補統治空間 , 那麼 , 那些被排除的弱者會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題我們等一下就會回到這問題上
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個信息是 , 如果你要傳遞這些亂流的次數或多或少 , 那麼 , 我們成功的做法 , 將取決於我們把合理的統治權帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	並且看著這一切開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和觀眾談這類的事情 , 但權力不只是直向移轉 , 還會橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你或許會說這個故事 , 文明的歷史 , 已經和第一批登上海的文明聚集在大西洋附近的海洋中 , 越近距離 , 西方的大西洋新國度就越高 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在正目睹了權力的根本轉變 , 廣義來說 , 遠離那些聚集在大西洋岸邊的國家 , 到那些聚集在太平洋岸邊的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	那從經濟實力開始 , 但那是開端 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外國政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增在世界上其他日益增長的政權中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為這其實不是很大的轉變 , 從西方轉到東方 , 不一樣的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 美國在接下來的十年、十五年間 , 仍然是世界上最強的國家 , 但她權力的背景現在已經徹底改變了 ; 這樣的情況已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正要走出五十年 , 最不尋常的歷史 , 在這個歷史上 , 我們已經有一個完全獨立的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每一方同情的需求 , 都必須被它的位置所參考 , 去華盛頓這個世界 , 由一個巨人所推崇 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但歷史上卻不是常見的案例 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在浮現的就是歷史中較常見的例子 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多極世界的出現 ,
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會一直保持最強大的國家 , 但在越來越多的強國 , 他們會是世界上最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你開始看到在中國建立另一種權力中心 , 當然 , 我自己的猜想是 , 中國要追求偉大 , 並不是那麼順利 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	中國在自由經濟後 , 會開始民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度、巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你逐漸發現 , 實際上 , 對我們歐洲人而言 , 世界看起來越來越像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:一位偉大的英國外交大臣 , 坎寧閣下 , 曾形容它為 「 歐洲人的權力協調 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一個平衡點 , 一個輔助五方面的平衡
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是以平衡的形式呈現
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國就和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來建立對應的平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個被壟斷的世界中 , 你有固定的同盟國北約組織 , 華約組織 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	權力的對立意謂著固定的結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力多極化的情況就表示轉移和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	那就是我們要進入的世界 , 我們會越來越常看見我們的同盟國並不是固定不變的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	傑出的英國外交大臣坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會越來越常見到即使我們西方國家也會伸出援手 , 不得不伸出大西洋的舒適圈 , 與他人結盟 , 只要我們想在世上完成一些事情 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 光是西方國家是不夠的 , 我們就得帶著其他人進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們得把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我的猜測是伊拉克和阿富汗是西方國家最後一次嘗試自己做 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是我們已經達到了400年後的開端 , 我說400年後的鄂圖曼帝國的終點 , 終結了西方強權的霸權 , 西方的機構和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家能團結在一起 , 它就能提出和丟棄在世界各個角落 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以最近二次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 ,
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行、國際貨幣基金組織布雷頓森林機構 , 問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們得打電話進去
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造二十國集團
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我來為你們做個預測 , 預測可能會更嚇人 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑現在已經400年了 , 當時西方國家的權力已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會參與調停 , 世界各地的多邊調停 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	噢 , 爲什麽不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍貝雷特下服役 , 服役於藍旗下 , 服役於聯合國國的指令下 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11個人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	海軍對付索馬利亞海盜問題最大的海軍艦隊是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍的內容
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是慈悲主義的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	想要維持航道暢通
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們沒有共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但 , 和誰合作 , 在當下 , 我們共享共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是個全新的角度來看現在正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素則完全不同
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天 , 在我們現代的世界 , 因為有網際網路 , 因為人們在這裡談論過的各種事物 , 每件事都連結在一起 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是以國家、個人的身份 , 以一種前所未有的方式互相影響 , 前所未有 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的相互關係 , 嗯 , 那一直都存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的相互關係
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在 , 我們緊密地聯繫在一起 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你會得到墨西哥的豬流感 , 這是查爾斯戴高樂機場24小時後所面臨的問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒閉 , 大量崩潰
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原發生火災 , 非洲的食物暴動 。
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地、深深地相互連結著 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	也就是說 , 一個國家獨自行動的概念 , 不與他人建立連結 , 不與他人合作 , 不再是一個可行的主張 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動本身既不受限 , 也不受限於國家本身 , 也不足以控制自己的領土 , 因為各國以外的影響現在也開始影響到其內部會發生什麼事 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	當時我還是年輕的大兵 , 在大英帝國戰爭時期
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國國防部只關乎一件事:我們的軍隊多強 , 我們的空軍多厲害 , 我們的海軍多厲害 , 以及我們的盟友多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是敵人在圍牆外的時候 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人就在城牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在如果我想談談我國防部 , 我得和衛生署談談因為傳染疾病對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得和農業部長談談因為食物安全對我的安全造成威脅 , 我得和工業部談談因為高科技基礎設施的脆弱性現在是我們的敵人攻擊點 , 正如我們從網路戰爭上所看到的 , 我得和內政部談談談因為那些發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我國 , 發生在我們的家鄉 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再只和軍人和國防有關 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	是它的能力可以將整個機構關起來 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴我們一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建造 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 垂直的階級制度 , 分工的任務 , 指揮結構把錯誤的結構完全搞錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	各位女士先生們 , 你們在商業上都知道 , 我們這個時代的典範結構就是這個網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	是你網絡的能力很重要無論是你的政府內部還是外部
so here is ashdown's third law .	所以這裡是下面第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	對了 , 別問我第一條規律和第二定律 , 因為我還沒發明出來 , 第三定律總是比較好聽吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	下面的第三個法則是:在現代 , 所有事情都有關連的時代 , 對於你能做的 , 最重要的事情是你能與他人做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你的結構 , 最重要的一點是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊軍隊 , 不論你是企業人 , 是你的關鍵點 , 你的內臟 , 你和他人聯絡的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在工業上 , 你明白這一點 ; 政府沒有 。
but now one final thing .	但現在最後一件事 ,
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣 , 女士們先生們 , 我們現在就以一種前所未有的方式團結在一起 , 那也是我們彼此有相同的命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間──而且是有史以來第一次 , 集體防禦──這些在我們國家安全的概念一直支配著我們的東西 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落還要強 , 我就安全了 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我就安全了 , 我的聯盟 , 像是北約組織 , 比他們的同盟強 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	已經不再是
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	相互連結以及大規模殺傷性武器的出現 , 意味著我和敵人有著越來越多的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官在日內瓦和蘇聯協商時 , 在七○年代 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解我們和他們有著相同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北愛爾蘭因為雙方了解 , 零和遊戲是行不通的
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著相同的命運
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	阻礙著中東和平的其中一項要素是以色列和巴勒斯坦人都不了解他們和我們有著相同的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位女士、先生們 , 過去在這個時代 , 由有遠見的人和詩人提出 , 變成我們必須要認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 最後我將以一首
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•多恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 請不要給誰鈴聲 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	這句話是: 「 每個男人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我也參與著人類的生命 , 不去問鐘聲到底是誰 , 而是為此付出 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	給約翰•多恩一個建議道德
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們而言 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的一部分
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到延長壽命和健康的路徑 , danbuetner和團隊在研究世界上的 「 藍色慢活區 」 , 這些社區的長者和有vim和vigor住在記錄年齡的社區 。 在tedxtc , 他共享9個常見的飲食和生活方式的習慣 , 使他們延續一百歲 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuettner:如何活到一百+
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個叫做丹麥雙胞胎的研究證實在某種生物限制下人平均壽命約為10%
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他百分之九十是由生活方式決定
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式我們就能得出一個實際的公式來延長壽命
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人長壽的方程式是什麼他們大概說不出來
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南灘減肥法或阿金減肥法
you have the usda food pyramid .	有美國農業部的食物金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	歐茲博士告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實上 , 有很多的混淆關於真正幫助我們活得更久的更好 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	談到營養品 , 你該吃嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或白葵呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	並且有目的性地參與其中嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	心靈層面 ? 那我們如何看待社交層面呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們研究長壽的方法是與國家地理還有國家老化研究院合作找出四個人口確定地理上的定義
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後把一組專家帶進來 , 用理論說這些人的所作所為 , 提煉出跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我會告訴你們精華是什麼
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想要破除一些常見的迷思長壽的迷思
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是如果你認真努力活到一百歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 在美國只有五千分之一的人能活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國成長最快的人口 , 很難達到100 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們不是長壽的計劃 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們是被程式化的 , 被稱作繁衍成功 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起大學時
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家把這個詞稱為 「 成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 然後再下一代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在這種進化的效應完全消失後 ,
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是隻老鼠或是大象 , 或人類 , 在這兩者之間 , 這是同一個故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要活到一百歲 , 你不僅需要有非常好的生活方式 , 你還得抽中基因頭彩 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有一些治療方法可以幫助緩慢、反轉、甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要你的腦袋缺氧幾分鐘腦細胞就會死 , 從不復返
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太激烈 , 跪在膝上 , 腳軟骨也碎了 , 軟骨也不回來了 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用血小板衝上來 , 我們的阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事要出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , t.兆個 , 我們現在是討論國債的數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就轉一圈 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每次他們轉身時都會造成一些傷害 , 而這種傷害會增強 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數方式增長
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這就有點像當我們都有披頭四或老鷹合唱團的唱片我們會複製一份到錄音帶上再讓朋友抄襲那錄音帶很快地 , 世世代就聽起來像垃圾
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個六十五歲的人老化的速度比一個十二歲的人快一百二十五倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有什麼辦法可以減緩或停止老化 , 我到底在做什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約可用九十年 , 女人的能力又更多了一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在那條線的某處 , 我們會把大約十二年的壽命留在桌上 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年可以讓我們
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 多年來大多都不會出現慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些消失的時代 , 最好的方法就是看看世界各地的文化 , 實際上正在經歷的文化 , 讓人們活到一百歲的比率 , 比我們高出十倍 , 平均壽命預期多出十幾年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們第一個藍寶地在義大利海岸外約一百二十五英哩處 , 薩丁尼亞島上
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人 , 而是位於高地上 , 一個叫努奧羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們看到的是男性最長壽的區域 , 百歲人瑞的數目大約是美國的十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的人不僅活到一百歲而已他們還擁有非凡的活力
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍舊騎腳踏車去工作砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十歲的小夥子
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上可以回溯到大約基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是個與世隔絕的青銅文化
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是非常不孕的 , 它們主要是牧羊人 , 有時是規律的、低強度的身體活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要以植物為基礎 , 以他們帶到田裡的食物為基礎 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包叫做carta , 用硬幣做成的乳酪 , 這種乳酪來自青草餵養的動物所以 , 乳酪富含omega-3脂肪酸而非omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自穀物餵養的動物還有一種葡萄酒 , 它的多酚物質含量是世界所知的三倍
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但是我認為真正的秘密 , 在於他們如何組織他們的社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎二十四歲就到頂點了 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看那些廣告 ,
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你越老越公平 , 你的智慧就越高 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧你看不到運動畫刊的泳裝日曆而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不只對你的老化父母有益 , 能讓他們和家人更親近 , 而且平均壽命大約四到六年研究顯示 , 這也對那些家庭的孩童有益 , 他們的孩童有較低的死亡率和較低的疾病 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	那叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現地球另一端的第二個藍寶地 , 在東京南方約800英里 , 在琉球的群島上 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球實際上是一百六十一個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主島的北端 , 這是世界長壽的原點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是現存最老的女性群體 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	那裡的人有著世界上最長而無障礙的預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們擁有我們想要的
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們能活很久 , 通常在睡眠不足時死亡 , 非常快速 , 通常 , 我能告訴你 , 在做愛之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多快活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	五倍於美國的百歲人瑞
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的結腸癌和乳癌案例是美國這裡的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比例是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	而這個文化產生的事實表明他們有東西可以教我們
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為主的飲食富有多種顏色的蔬菜
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃大約八倍的豆腐比起美國人來說
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比牠們所吃的食物更為重要
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種小策略來避免過食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們會從較小的盤子上吃飯 , 所以在每次的座位吃的卡路里也較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其照顧家庭風格 , 你說話時 , 可以無意識地吃 , 他們在櫃台服役 , 把食物拿走 , 然後把食物送到桌子上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一句三千年的格言我認為是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議
it was invented by confucius .	由孔子所發明
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	那飲食就是大家所知的騷擾 , hatchi、butchi、
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是一小段話 , 這些人在用餐之前說 , 要提醒他們吃東西時 , 胃部滿了80% 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	飽足感要花半小時才能從肚子傳到腦袋 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住吃到八分飽就好幫助你不做這些事
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但就像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有些社會結構是我們能與長壽相關的 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會害死人 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前美國人平均有三個好朋友
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在減少到一半
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生在琉球你會生在一種體系裡讓你自動擁有半打朋友陪他們度過人生
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為模合 。 如果你處於某個模合你被期待分享假如你運氣好 , 孩子生病、父母去世 , 你總是會有某個人在背後支持你 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個 「 模合 」 , 這五位女士相處在一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是一百零二歲
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人生活分成兩部份 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	有我們的工作、有生產力的地方 ,
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 碰 , 我們退休
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這表示要退休去坐簡單的椅子 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語裡甚至沒有退休這個詞
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	反之 , 有一個詞散播了你的一生 , 這個詞是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗略的翻譯是 「 早上醒來的理由 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位一百零二歲的空手道師父來說他的生存價值就是拿著這件武術
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 一週還會繼續捕魚 ,
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	而這是個問題 。 國家老化研究院實際給了我們一份問卷 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們在文化上非常敏銳 , 那些問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的生存價值是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上醒來 ,
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老太太來說 , 她的生存價值只是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位分別待在一百零一歲半的女孩
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著曾曾曾孫女的身分 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回來 , 說: 「 這感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這想法很棒 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要我找到美國的藍寶地 ,
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們去看明尼蘇達的草原那裡的百歲人瑞的比例非常高
but that's because all the young people left .	但是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的兒童族群是基督復臨安息日會的基督徒集中在加州的羅馬林達市
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派是保守的教徒
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日落日當天向日落慶祝安息日
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四小時的避難所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	而且他們遵循五個小習慣 , 相對來說 , 是傳達他們非凡的長壽 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國這裡 , 女性的平均壽命是80 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但基督復臨派的女教友她們的預期壽命是89
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯他們預期能多活十一年比起美國同伴來說
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究.而且我認為這可以說是這個藍寶地計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個異質的族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共有的是一套生活小習慣他們一生中大部分時間都遵從儀式式 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中拿取飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀第一章第二十九節上帝談到豆子和種子另一個是談到綠色植物很明顯少了肉
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個避難所 ,
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時不管有多忙 , 工作壓力有多大 , 孩子需要被推動去工作 , 他們停止一切 , 專注於他們的上帝、他們的社交網路 , 然後 , 在宗教的那一刻 , 都是大自然的走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這種力量並不是偶爾在完成的 , 力量是每週持續一生的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	基督復臨派教徒往往跟其他教徒來往
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個基督復臨派的聚會 , 你不會看到人們揮舞著吉姆beam或打滾一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在說下一次的自然步行交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻且可測的方式互相影響著彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化造就了埃爾斯沃•偉倫這樣的人
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是千萬富翁可是當包商想要六千美金來建造隱私的圍籬時他說: 「 為了那樣的錢 , 我會自己去做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	接下來的三天 , 他都在外頭鏟水泥 , 把柱子拖來拖去 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預料 , 也許在第四天他就進手術室了 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上這個人而是做開心手術的人
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	97歲的他仍然每個月做20次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在一百零三歲 , 一位活躍的牛仔 , 早上才開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	週末他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 扔出公雞尾酒 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實就住在雙子城這裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	一天開始 , 她舉重 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎著腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	然後 , 她在1994年的塞維利亞卡提卡路里 , 流下了聖博納迪諾的高速公路 , 在那裡她仍然是志工服務七個不同的組織 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加十九次冒險活動 ,
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一你見過的人中唯一一個騎著腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠沒有防曬霜
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比和馬奇•戴頓合作更恐怖的了 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 一個陌生人是一個我還沒遇見的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都在做些什麼呢 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功的把它歸結為九項
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自此之後 , 我們又進行了兩次藍色地帶探險 , 並且這些共同的探險家持有的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	而第一個 , 我快要說了 , 這裡沒有一個是運動 , 至少是我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們安排他們的生活 , 讓他們不斷地被推入身體的活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人她們坐在地板上 , 起身又坐下一天三、四十回
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店或教堂或去朋友家都要走路
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕要去做院子工作或屋子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想攪拌蛋糕 , 他們會用手
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里跟跑步機一樣多
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們進行刻意的身體活動時 , 這是他們所享受的東西 。 他們傾向行走 , 這是唯一證實能延遲認知能力的衰退 , 他們往往有一個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式安排他們的生活 , 這樣他們才有正確的外觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都花時間在降低 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 教徒祈禱
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人敬祖
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你趕時間或壓力大 , 會引發一種發炎反應 , 這種反應跟很多病相關 , 從老年癡呆症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你每天放慢15分鐘 , 就會把那個發炎狀態變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	它們的字彙有目的感、生存感 , 像琉球人的 「 生者 」 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道自己生命中最危險的兩年是出生那年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率還有退休那年
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的使命感 , 並在生活中活躍起來 , 那價值大約是七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反地 , 這些人每天都喝一點點酒 , 賣給美國人並不難 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們往往以植物為主的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是吃很多豆類跟堅果
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有阻止過度飲食的策略一些在對的時間將他們推離桌面的小東西
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 這一切的基礎是他們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人擺第一照顧好小孩跟年邁父母
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全都屬於一個信仰型的社群 , 這價值四到十四年額外的預期壽命假如你一個月四次的話 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	其中最嚴重的是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就愛死他們 , 就是積極地繞著自己 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知如果你三個最好的朋友都胖你有一半的機率會變胖
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 假如你跟不健康的人來往隨著時間就會有明顯的影響
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你朋友的休閒想法是體力活動 , 保齡球 , 或是打曲棍球、騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝一點酒 , 但不多 , 他們吃得正當 , 他們吃得正當 , 他們很投入 , 且值得信任和值得信賴 , 會隨著時間而產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	節食是沒有用的 。 世界歷史上沒有一個飲食可以讓超過百分之二的人口都工作過 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月開始十月就完成
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	講到長壽在避孕藥丸上或其他的用詞都不存在 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但 , 想想看 , 你的朋友都是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做最有意義的事 , 來為你的生活增添更多年 。 多謝你 。 非常感謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水來導電 ; 一扇窗由清晰轉向不透明 , 打開關 ; 製造音樂的果凍 。 所有這些東西都有 。 卡翠娜.莫塔說:是時候該玩了 。 莫塔帶我們去巡迴新素材 , 提醒我們 , 我們能為它們找到好處 , 做實驗、修改、有趣的 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	卡塔琳娜.莫塔:玩弄智慧型材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機搭了一台車這樣他就可以載送家人
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做既是因為沒錢買車還是因為他知道如何建車
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間 , 我們了解東西是如何運作的 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 所以我們能夠建造和修理它們 , 或至少明智地知道該買什麼的決定 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	許多diy的做法自二十世紀下半葉起失傳
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 創建者社群以及開放模型正將東西的運作及其成份帶回我們生活中而我相信我們需要更進一步去了解事物的組成
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的情況下 , 我們仍然知道紙和紡織品等傳統原料是由什麼製成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些令人驚嘆又有未來感的複合材料塑膠能夠改變形狀 , 能導電的顏料還有會改變顏色的顏料還有會發光的布料
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們不需要用傳統印刷電路或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上的這個小例子 , 我們用它來建立一個觸控感應器 , 透過打開這個小光就能感應我的皮膚 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家一直都在使用導電油墨 , 但最近的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能將它用在雷射印表機和筆上面 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這塊丙烯酸纖維附滿了無色的散光粒子
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的丙烯酸纖維只會在邊緣散光但這一塊散光整個表面當我開燈的時候
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這項材料有兩個已知的應用 , 包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱變色顏料則會在特定溫度下變色
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我要把這個東西放在一個裝在溫度上的熱板上 , 只比環境溫度稍高一點點 , 你就能知道會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 其它東西可以表示內容物是否涼了可以喝了 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是我們所知的智慧型材料中的一部分 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	再過幾年 , 它們就會出現在我們每天使用的許多物品和技術中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法擁有科幻小說中會出現的飛天汽車但我們可以有改變顏色的牆壁根據溫度 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤還有在開關上變得不透明的窗戶
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	所以我是個社會科學家 , 為什麼我今天要來這裡談論智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我對東西的運作和製造方式感到好奇 , 也是因為我相信我們應該要對構成我們世界的這些元素有更深入的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對這些將來會做的高科技複合材料的了解還不夠 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以在少量下取得
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	關於如何使用它們 , 幾乎沒有任何的資訊被拿來使用 , 很少有人說它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 它們大部分都存在於貿易秘密和專利的領域中 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年多前 , 我和克絲蒂•波義耳開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為材料公開 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	在這個網站中 , 我們以及任何其他想加入的人都可以分享實驗成果、發表資訊鼓勵別人隨時都可以貢獻一己之力並聚集研究資源比如說研究論文及輔導其他像我們一樣的製作者
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個大型、集體自行生成的資料庫 , 以便智慧型材料使用 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但是為什麼我們應該要關心智慧型材料的運作方式以及組成呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 最後卻用不懂的東西塑造我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品 , 穿的衣服住的房子 , 全都對我們的行為健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們生活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該認識並理解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 同樣重要的是創新總是以修補匠的形式在推動著
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 而不是專家 , 一直都是登山自行車的發明者和改進者 , 包括半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學很複雜 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但不見得總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學有兩名科學家便瞭解這一點 , 當他們發表一篇論文時 , 用來製作導電油墨的方法比較簡單 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	喬登邦克在那之前完全沒有相關化學經驗 , 讀了這篇論文 , 然後在他的自造者空間複製實驗 , 用的只是現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱甚至根據其他科學家的說明書自製試管震盪器
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登後來在網路上公佈了他的研究結果 , 包含他已經嘗試過的所有事情 , 且沒有成功的結果 , 讓其他人可以研究並進行繁殖 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 喬登創新的主要形式是把一項實驗在設備精良的大學實驗室中進行 , 並在芝加哥的車庫中重現它 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己變成那樣 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項成果 , 其他人可以去查詢他離開的地方 , 設計更簡單的流程和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	我想提到的另一個例子是強調材料的表達特質 , 同時專注於建造者的創意和技巧 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子零件非常強大 , 他們教導我們物件如何運作 , 但設計上的限制與生俱來也會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的做法是規劃一系列的技術用來創造出不尋常的物品使我們能不受限於設計上的限制只要教導我們有關材料本身的知識
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以漢娜眾多令人印象深刻的實驗裡 , 這是我最喜歡的作品之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面貼了一些銅線 , 連到mp3播放器和磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究漢娜用各式各樣的材料製作出一系列的紙喇叭口說從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布和油墨
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像喬登以及許多其它的製作者漢娜將她的食譜公開讓任何人可以複製、繁殖
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子只是現在前景最被看好的材料科學其中一個分支讓我們能創造出更便宜、靈活的電子
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的手工藝成品 , 以及她分享發現的事實 , 為一系列新的可能性打開了一扇美感上訴和創新的門 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們的熱情和好奇心所創造出來的 , 且我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常從不守規矩的角度來處理問題 , 過程中 , 最後會發現替代方案 , 甚至是更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人在材料上做實驗越多研究人員願意分享研究散播知識製造商就越有機會創造出服務眾人的科技
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以 , 我覺得有點像泰德尼爾森在一九七零年代早期 , 他寫道: 「 現在你必須要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是只有科學家在關心的大架構 , 甚至沒有人夢想能在家裡安裝一個 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 我現在站在這裡說得有點奇怪 , 「 你們現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	只要記住 , 取得關於新興科技的先發知識是確保我們在創造未來能有發言權的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入玻璃泡泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 仰賴我們的眼睛來引導我們 , 即使我們只能看見前方和後方的幾輛車 。 但如果汽車可以彼此分享他們的位置和速度 , 並且使用預測模型來計算路上每個人最安全的路徑 ? 珍妮佛•希里想像一個沒有發生意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•喜利:如果車子可以說話意外可能是可以避免的
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但現實中 , 宗教圖標和好運文法會出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲青年死亡的主因車禍是導致死亡的主因而百分之七十五的車禍和毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說 , 但我記得我第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	當時我還年輕在高速公路上 , 前面的車輛 , 我看到煞車燈亮了起來 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在停車 , 停車 , 在高速公路上停車 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65比0嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我猛踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	abs系統啟動了但車仍向前駛車繼續向前我知道車不會停了氣囊彈出車子毀了幸好沒有人受傷
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到那輛車會停我認為我們可以做得更好
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛體驗 , 只要讓我們的車子互相交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只希望各位回想一下現在開車的體驗是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上車關上門 , 你在玻璃的泡泡裡
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的軀殼裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是在看不清路面的情況下在其他金屬巨人之間以超人的速度在行駛 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	可以嗎 ? 而你只需要引導你的是你的兩眼 。
