okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 這就是你唯一擁有的 , 眼睛不是針對這項任務來設計的 , 但後來有人請你做類似的事情 , 你想改寫車道 , 他們問你的第一件事情是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	離開路面後的眼睛 。 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要再看你前進的方向 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開下車不去看你前進的方向 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他所有人 。 這是安全駕駛的方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須 , 我們要做出選擇 , 我是要看這裡還是這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們在路上做了一個很棒的工作──挑選我們要走的路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯過一些事情 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們感知到不對或太遲的事 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 駕駛說: 「 我沒看到它要來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我也相信 , 我也相信
we can only watch so much .	我們只能觀看這麼多
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現存的科技可以幫助我們改善這個狀況 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了汽車互相交換數據 , 我們不僅可以看到前面三部輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 右邊和左邊 , 同時間 , 鳥瞰視野 , 我們還將能實際觀察到這些車 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們將能看見前方車輛的速度看得多快或停止
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那傢伙打算減到零 , 我就會知道
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	透過計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能覺得這不可能
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你如何能預測未來 ? 那真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不是 。 有汽車 , 不是不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車輛是立體的有固定的位置和速度
they travel down roads .	沿著路行駛 ,
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在預先出版的路線上行駛 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來在哪裡 , 真的不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	就算你在你的車上 , 和一些摩托車騎士是bshoom ! 以85英里的時速飛行 , 我知道你有這段經驗 , 並不是 「 那傢伙無中生有 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙可能在路上開了半個小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看到他 ,
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10哩前20哩前30哩前 , 一定有人看到那傢伙 , 一旦看到那傢伙 , 把他放到地圖上 , 他就在地圖上 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度持續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車會在他耳邊小聲說: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車手 , 小心 ! 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測車子的行為
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對牠們很好 ,
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 就好比在汽車之間分享我們車與車之間的位置資料 , 只要分享gps就行了 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車上裝有gps和攝影機 , 我就能精確地知道我在哪裡 , 以及我有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估算我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 以及他們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己身在何方也能模糊地看待其他車子的位置
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩個車子分享這些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會如何 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以確切地告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了一個電腦模擬看下列情況會產生什麼結果當用輕微的方式估計當汽車只要分享gps資訊我們將這研究從電腦模擬帶到裝有汽車的機械試驗設備用在車上:立體攝影機、gps還有平面雷射雷射雷射雷射雷射雷射雷射雷射探測器這些都是普遍的配備
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還裝上一台短距的無線電機台 , 機械人彼此聊天 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些飛行器朝向對方靠近時 , 它們會追蹤到彼此的精確位置 , 它們能避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在混合當中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你的演講太多時 , 很難去處理所有的資料封包 , 所以你得優先順序 , 這就是預測模型會幫助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你就不會去注意那些格子 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	把這個看起來有點偏差的傢伙列為優先順序 ,
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能會是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	就可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離航道 , 要知道怎麼做 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道哪些駕駛要提高警覺 , 才能擺脫這條路 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼樣警告所有人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車要怎麼小聲地說: 「 你得趕緊離開 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一是汽車的能力 , 第二是駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有一個人擁有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們是在用手機 , 或者 , 你知道的 , 做些什麼 , 他們可能沒有在緊急時刻做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	因此 , 我們開始一個獨立的研究專門做駕駛者的狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用三部攝影機 , 我們可以偵測司機在看向前看 , 看下 , 看手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外狀況 , 並預測誰是誰 , 哪一部車是最好的狀態 , 來離開 , 讓每個人計算出最安全的路徑 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些科技在今日仍然存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願去分享我們的數據 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這個想法讓人十分不安這個想法是 , 我們的車子會監視我們 , 跟其他車子談談我們 , 我們會在一片流言密語的大海中沿路行進 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我看著你的車從外面看 , 我對你不太了解 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看著你的牌照號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們背後討論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而且我覺得這會是一件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望各位思考一下 , 如果你真的不希望那煩人的青少年在你背後知道你要煞車 , 知道你要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	很願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以做到對每個人最好的一件事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以讓你的車子八卦你
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize公司彼得.戴曼迪斯談到他是如何協助史蒂芬霍金實現他前往太空的夢想 , 透過飛到上層大氣層 , 體驗到零g的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短話題、空間、科技、宇宙、
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	史蒂芬•霍金斯的彼得•戴曼迪斯0gro 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道 , 我對於開創太空新領域有多麼熱衷 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 那真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他是在基因學archonxprize的場合上 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們現在所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一個在十天內完成100個人類基因組定序的團隊 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有一種叫做 「 基因體一百 」 的東西 , 是我們用來定序的一百個人 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特是那個活動的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是上太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你上去 , 但我可以帶你體重為零 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他當場就說: 「 沒錯 , 是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 要體驗zerog的唯一方法事實上是用拋物線飛行 , 沒有重量飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	搭一架飛機 , 飛過頂點 , 兩十五秒都沒有重量 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 你的重量加倍 。
you do it again and again .	一而再 , 再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到八、十分鐘的無重力──美國太空總署訓練他們多久的太空人的方式 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了十一年才營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	然後我們宣布將要搭載史蒂芬•霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一個政府機關及飛機操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你要殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	而他想要去
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們舉辦了記者會 , 我們宣佈我們打算做一個無重力拋物線飛行 , 給他25秒的無重力 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切進行得非常順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他 , 為什麼他要過去做這個 ?
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他所說的話 , 對我來說 , 非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生物面臨著不斷增加的危機可能會被災難所消滅...
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不上太空的話 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他去甘迺迪太空中心 , 在nasa的車內 , 走到zero-g飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們總共有大約20個人捐款我們募到了15萬美元作為兒童慈善事業之用他們跟著我們一起飛
a few tedsters here .	這裡幾位tedsters
we set up a whole er .	我們建立了整個急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他血液的po2值、心跳、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	萬一緊急事件 , 我們什麼都發生了 。 天知道 , 你不會想傷害這位舉世聞名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 太空梭起降的地方降落 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我的夥伴byronlichtenberg跟我小心的把他暫停為零
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他到了那裡 , 我們就讓他體驗無重力真正的樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	經過第一個拋物線飛行後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他笑了 , 然後我們說去 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實讓一顆漂浮著的蘋果 , 向艾薩克•牛頓爵士致敬 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋也舉辦了相同的椅子 , 那是艾薩克•牛頓爵士所做的 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	和第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	而這個人看上去一點也不像65歲的輪椅人 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們住在一顆珍貴的珠寶上 , 它是在我們的有生之年 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請與我們一同參加這趟壯舉般的冒險之旅 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師davidbolinsky呈現了3分鐘的驚人動畫 , 呈現的是細胞內的動畫 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、醫療、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛•布林斯基對一個細胞進行動畫 。
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學繪圖師 , 我的觀點和別人稍微不同 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察藝術中真與美的表現方式 , 以及科學中真與美的表現方式 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然兩者都是很美好的事物它們本身都有美好的東西將之視為理想的事物可以被科學和數學所檢視的事物就像是理想的連體雙胞胎他們想要與科學家約會的那種
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些 「 真 」 的表達方式是敬畏的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 , 不可或缺的
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時它們有用 , 通常很久之後才會出現 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你們可以播放其中一些照片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看到我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美常常對不在科學界的人而言 , 真與美往往是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們被描述成美的方式 , 通常只有在你了解了這個主題的人所使用的語言和語法時 , 才會出現這種美麗的描述 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你仔細觀察數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你觀察宇宙常數 , 在宇宙中 , 有著一個人類理想的理想 , 你會發現生命必須從描述宇宙的數字演化而來──這些是非常難以理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我當醫學繪圖師的經驗以來 , 我就試著去做一件事──自從我被教導要動畫時 , 我父親是一位雕塑家和視覺導師──我想找出一種方法 , 幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美──藉由動畫、使用圖片、講述故事 , 讓人們不見得有證據的事物 , 能夠被傳授、教導 , 並且能夠被了解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常沉浸在一種環境中 , 在這種環境中 , 他們所學習到的事物中 , 有著真與美 , 但他們被教導的方式是分層式的 , 且被歸類為事實和美麗並不總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像是煮雞湯的陳年食譜 , 煮雞肉直到香味通通散去 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣對待我們的學生 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子與細胞生物學系的robertlue的電話幾年前 , 他問我我和我的團隊是否有興趣真正改變哈佛大學的醫學與科學教育程度
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個探索細胞的計畫 , 來探索分子與細胞生物學中固有的真與美 , 讓學生能夠了解一個更大的圖片 , 讓他們可以把這些事實掛在上面 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們腦海中可以想像細胞是一座大型繁忙複雜的城市 , 由微機械組成 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 能讓全世界的奈米工程師嫉妒 , 它們能自我引導、強大且精確的裝置 , 都是用胺基酸串連而成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	而這些微機械會驅動細胞的移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們驅動了細胞複製、激發我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們能驅動我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 想辦法讓這個故事成爲動畫 , 這將是哈佛大學biovisions的主軸 , 它是一個哈佛大學為分子與細胞生物學學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有文字訊息以外的物件 , 所有東西都被視覺化 , 這樣這些學生可以從內化的視覺化的觀點來了解細胞的真與美 , 並且能夠在腦海中學習 , 以這些觀點去發揮他們的想像力 , 以外 , 如此他們就能在腦海中找到新思想的原理 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子的組合方式 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們研究的主題是巨噬細胞會沿著微血管流動 , 它們會觸碰到微血管壁表面 , 它們會取得微血管壁上細胞的資訊 , 它們會從微血管壁上提取資訊 , 它們會把資訊給呈現在外面某處的發炎資訊 , 在那裡 , 它們無法被看見、感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的信息是導致他們停止的 , 使他們內化 , 必須製造各式各樣的零件 , 使他們改變形狀 , 並且試著跳出這微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛大學的科學家合作 , 以及資料庫模型 , 看出原子上的正確分子 , 找出它們如何移動 , 看出它們做了什麼 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	並想出如何以真理去做這件事 , 藉由它導入了正在發生的事情 , 但不是這麼真實 , 以致於細胞中的小規模擁擠將避免發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	我現在要給你們看的是我們製作的這個影片的第一個版本的三分鐘讀者的消化版本 。 這是一個持續進行的企劃將經過四到五年的時間 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這個現象 , 看看細胞製造這些走路的小機械 , 它們叫做驅動蛋白 , 將巨大的負載量大到相對大小的螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請繼續看這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器是非常驚人的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會互相傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們導致細胞內發生不同的事 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會製造果蠅需要的部位 , 藉由讀取基因的分子 , 從細胞核中產生的信息 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每個人 , 若沒有這些小小的微機械 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , chris的出席率是相當零散的 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞中的fedex快遞小傢伙 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 他把一袋新製造出來的蛋白質拉到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是到細胞膜上 , 不論是用來做某物或修補 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬個這種東西可以跑來跑去 , 就在現在 , 在你一百兆個細胞當中 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 本質上 , 你並沒有在做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 回家後 , 我希望各位能想想這一點 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到的一些關於細胞機械的知識 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們了解全部的狀況 , 相信我 , 我們就會知道 , 一旦我們搞清楚狀況 , 幾乎是百分之一的狀況 , 我們就真的能夠掌控我們用健康的方式 , 用我們後代的努力 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能藉此發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很不可思議 , 它們知道細胞需要什麼在它們身上執行什麼功能 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起合作 。 它們使細胞完成它所需要做的 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們一起合作 , 幫助我們的身體──巨大的實體──它們永遠無法察覺它們的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	請繼續欣賞接下來的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪布蘭頓在她的貨車上計畫住了一年 , 看到這個國家 , 但當憂鬱開始 , 且她的自由工作結束時 , 她的露營旅行變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演說中 , 她描述了她成為美國無家可歸者的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、幸福、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會變遷、社會、說故事等 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:那一年我無家可歸
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家也是記者 , 我也是個超有好奇心的人 , 所以在22年 , 身為記者 , 我學會了很多新事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學懂的其中一件事就是當個隱世人
i became one of the working homeless .	我成了一名工作無家可歸者 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作就在我父親同年二月去世之後我決定去旅行
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的去世對我打擊很大
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當我在做這件事時 , 我有很多想要感覺和處理的事 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我這一生都在露營我決定在旅行車中生活一年就像一趟漫長的露營旅行
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我把我的貓 , 我的洛威爾和我的露營裝備塞進了一台1975年雪佛蘭小貨車上 , 開車到日落裡 , 完全沒有發現三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:社會把生活在一個永久的結構中 , 甚至是一個小木屋裡 , 與人的價值感劃上等號 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到 , 很快地 , 其他人的負面觀感會影響我們的現實 , 如果我們任由它來 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車很棒 ,
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 我定期在外用餐
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我還有時間休息和哀悼
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親過世時的憤怒和沮喪開始了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須找全職來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	本來溫和的春天卻轉變為極熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	更不可能停車 , 完全不明白我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 牠真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓從車窗來回走
the doggy went into doggy day care .	道奇隊進入日間護理中心
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能夠使用辦公大樓和卡車站的員工淋浴間 ,
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或在公共休息室洗身
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下讓人幾乎無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在高溫下腐壞
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰粒 , 數小時之內就融化了 , 而且還蠻悲慘的 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我沒錢找到一間公寓 , 或是買不起能讓我擁有羅特威爾和貓的公寓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	而我拒絕放棄他們所以我繼續住在旅行車裡
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當夜間的高溫讓我連走五十英尺的公共洗手間 , 我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度降到零度以下 , 還留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我也面臨了全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都把一個不同的地方停下來 , 避免被警察察察察覺到 , 被警察騷擾 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感覺失控了我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我從一個才華橫溢的作家和記者 , 變成一個住在旅行車裡的無家可歸女子 , 把我的呼吸帶走了 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	那時我還沒變 , 我的智商沒降
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的正直、我的價值觀 , 關於我的一切 , 都還是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我不知怎地改變了
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在沮喪中越鑽越深 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我轉到無家可歸的健康診所
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	然後我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊中任何人一樣臭味和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有喝醉或喝得高 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當許多流浪漢發現 , 包括一個以前的大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的 。 你為什麼會在這裡呢 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者不把我當成無家者 , 但我做到了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	那教授聽完我的故事後 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者是沒有希望的 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的這種憂鬱症的反應 , 讓我有了自殺傾向 。 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我自殺了 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 一個朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•羅斯一個全國著名的記者在全國廣播電台上跟我談過 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我曾寫過一篇關於我父親的文章 , 就在他死前一年 , 在提姆的新書上 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在做一個講稿聯播節目 。 他在說我正在寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我發現提姆羅素 , 《與傳媒會見》前主持人談到我寫作 , 當時我住在旅行車上停在沃爾瑪超市的停車場 , 我開始大笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了因為它到達了我是作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那 , 重新讀一次自己的文章
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久我搬回了田納西
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我在旅行車上和朋友住在家鄉的沙發上做交替
and i started writing again .	然後我又重新開始寫作
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	第二年夏天 , 我是一名工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我是贏得獎項的 , 住在我自己的公寓裡
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數千人全職工作兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續歧視和犯罪 , 繼續住在車上或在街上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家可歸的人、無家者 , 主要還是維持看不見 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到他們 , 讓他們投入、鼓勵他們、給他們希望
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的心靈可以克服一切事物 , 只要它有希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡當 「 無家可歸 」 的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個乞討者 ,
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡、睡哪裡 , 或是生活中的狀況 , 都不是依據我的經驗 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在旅行車上停在沃爾瑪超市的停車場內而今天我在ted演講
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望永遠都能找到路 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaidya , 帶領我們走過全國的大膽計畫 , 從1970年代開始 , 提高人們的生活水準 。 第一步是:人口控制 。 這就表示 , 許多法蘭克 , 有趣的 , 和非常有效的談論安全套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	mechaiviravaidya:如何保險套讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有很多人生活在貧窮的環境中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定針對此點下手 , 但我們不是從福利方案開始 , 也不是貧窮減少計畫 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從節育計畫開始 , 遵循非常成功的婦女健康活動 , 一系列的活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以基本上 , 沒有人會接受節育計畫 , 如果孩子沒有存活下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:先去找孩童 , 先去找母親 , 然後再做家庭計畫 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩童死亡率 , 你還需要節育計畫 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶大家回到我們為什麼需要做這件事 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 1974年也是如此 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有七個孩子都有很大的成長率 , 成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	完全沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	我們就說: 「 就去做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女們說: " 我們也同意 , 我們會用避孕藥 , 但我們需要醫生來幫我們開藥 。 " 我們的醫生很少 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不接受 「 不 」 的答案 ; 我們不接受 「 不 」 的問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去看護士和助產士 , 他們也是女人 , 在解釋如何使用避孕藥上做得很棒 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	聽起來很棒 , 但它只涵蓋了全國20%的人口 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	至於其他80%的人 , 我們該怎麼做才能讓他們獨自一人 , 並說: 「 嗯 , 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去找了你們看到的普通人 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那黃色標誌下 , 我希望他們沒有擦掉 , 因為那邊有 「 可口可樂 」 的標誌 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	那個年代 , 我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒有差別 , 他們所選的人是我們所選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道顧客永遠是對的 , 他們很棒 , 他們自己做家庭規劃 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	這樣他們就可以供應藥丸和保險套遍及全國各地 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以 , 我們在那裡 。 我們去了那些被視為問題解決方案的起因的人 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論那裡有人 , 你可以看到船上有女性 , 這裡出售東西是漂浮市場 , 這裡賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有各種避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡找到人 , 你都會在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 為什麼不找宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會的信仰很強壯 , 而泰國人都是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我在那邊是穿藍色衣服的 , 不是黃色的 , 手上拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶把聖水灑在避孕藥和保險套上 , 以保險套神聖的神聖 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片傳遍了整個國家 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村莊的僧侶自己也在做同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	婦女們都說: " 難怪我們沒有副作用 ,
it's been blessed . "	原來是有福的 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的認知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們找上教師
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每一個人參與試著提供任何能讓人類變得更好的東西 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師們 ,
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	有超過25萬人受教於節育計畫用新的字母a、b生育、c代表保險套、子宮切除術等等
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有了蛇和梯子遊戲 , 讓你投擲骰子 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你停在任何應有的計劃上 , 你就往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如說: 「 媽媽每晚都吃這藥丸 ,
very good , mother . move ahead .	非常好 , 母親 。 向前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	舅舅買保險套 。 非常好 , 舅舅 。 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	舅舅喝醉了 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 再開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育 , 階級娛樂
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們也在學校辦到了 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們有使用保險套的接力賽道 , 有著兒童保險套的冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	不久後 , 保險套成為女孩的最好朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮苦人家來說 , 鑽石不會這樣做的所以保險套才是女孩的好朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個小額貸款計畫 , 主辦計畫的婦女說: 「 我們只想借錢給有執行節育計畫的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 就照顧好懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們這裡貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	而那是他們所為 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在三十五/三十六年後 , 它仍然持續進行著 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村子發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 但它是基金的小額貸款 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來經營它 , 由村民自己來經營 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你可能很難在那看到一個泰國男子 , 總有女人 , 女人 , 女人 ,
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	後來我們認為我們會幫助美國 , 因為美國一直在幫助每一個人 , 無論他們是否願意幫助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	而這是7月4日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供輸精管切除術 , 但尤其是 , 排在隊列前的美國男性 , 排在大使隊的駐守期間 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	旅館給了我們一間球場 , 非常適合 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	由於午餐時間差不多 , 他們說: 「 好吧 , 我們來點午餐 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 那一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	你會得到兩個品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	食物方面是漢堡或熱狗二選一 。 」
and i thought a hotdog will be more symbolic .	而我認為熱狗比較有象徵意義 。
and here is this , then , young man called willy bohm who worked for the usaid .	接下來是這位年輕人 , 名叫威利.博希 , 他替美國國際開發總署工作 。
obviously , he's had his vasectomy because his hotdog is half eaten , and he was very happy .	很明顯的 , 他得了輸精管切除術 , 因為他的熱狗有一半被吃掉了 , 而且他非常開心 。
it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	它在美國做了很多新聞 , 同時也激怒了一些人 。
i said , " don't worry . come over and i'll do the whole lot of you . "	我說: 「 別擔心 , 過來找我就跟你們一樣 。 」
in all this thing , from seven children to 1 . 5 children , population growth rate of 3 . 3 to 0 . 5 .	所有這一切 , 從7個孩子到1.5個孩子 , 人口成長率是3.3到0.5個 。
you could call it the cocacola approach if you like it was exactly the same thing .	你也可以稱它為可口可樂法如果你喜歡它是完全一樣的東西
i'm not sure whether cocacola followed us , or we followed cocacola , but we're good friends .	我不太確定是不是可口可樂跟隨我們 , 或是我們追隨可口可樂 , 但我們是好朋友 。
and so that's the case of everyone joining in .	所以每個人都要加入這個行列 。
we didn't have a strong government . we didn't have lots of doctors .	我們沒有強大的政府 , 沒有很多醫生
but it's everybody's job who can change attitude and behavior .	但是每個人都可以改變態度和行為 。
then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病襲擊泰國 , 我們得要停止做許多好事來對抗愛滋病 。
but unfortunately , the government was in denial , denial , denial .	但不幸的是 , 政府是否認可、否認
so our work wasn't affected .	所以我們的工作沒有受到影響 。
so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	於是我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能到政府那裡 , 就去從軍吧 。 」
so i went to the military and asked to borrow 300 radio stations .	所以我去拜訪軍方 , 要求借300個電台 。
they have more than the government , and they've got more guns than the government .	他們擁有的槍多過政府 , 而且擁有的槍也比政府多
so i asked them , could they help us in our fight against hiv .	所以我問他們 , 能不能協助我們對抗愛滋病毒 。
and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我給他們統計數字後 , 他們說: 「 好的 。 你可以使用所有的電台、電視台 。 」

and then we got a new prime minister soon after that .	之後沒多久 , 我們又找了一位新的總理

he became the chairman of the national aids committee and increased the budget fiftyfold .	他成為了國家愛滋病委員會的主席 , 並且提高了預算的50倍 。
every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每一個部長 , 甚至法官 , 都必須接受愛滋病的教育 。 每一個人 , 我們都說公開、機構、宗教機構、學校 , 每一個人都參與其中 。
and here , every media person had to be trained for hiv .	在這裡 , 每一個媒體人都需要接受愛滋病毒的培訓 。

so they were happy with that .	所以他們對此很滿意 。
and then aids education in all schools , starting from university .	接著 , 所有學校都有愛滋病的教育 , 從大學開始 。
and these are high school kids teaching high school kids .	而這些高中生在教高中生
and the best teachers were the girls , not the boys , and they were terrific .	最棒的老師是女孩子們 , 不是男孩 , 她們都很棒 。
and these girls who go around teaching about safe sex and hiv were known as mother theresa .	而這些到處教導安全性愛和愛滋病的女孩則被稱為德蕾莎修女 。
and then we went down one more step .	然後我們再往下一步 ,
these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三年級、四年級的孩子 , 去村裡的每個家庭、在整個泰國的每個家庭 , 提供愛滋病資訊和保險套給每一個家庭 , 給這些小孩子 。
and no parents objected , because we were trying to save lives , and this was a lifesaver .	沒有家長反對 , 因為我們試圖拯救生命 , 這是救命仙丹 。

and then we gave condoms out everywhere on the streets everywhere , everywhere .	然後我們在街上發放保險套 , 每一個角落都有 。

and also , in traffic , the policemen give you condoms our " cops and rubbers " programs .	還有 , 在交通中 , 警察會給你保險套──我們的 「 警察和橡皮屋 」 計畫 。
so , can you imagine new york policemen giving out condoms ?	所以 , 你能想像紐約警察發給你保險套嗎 ?

but let me warn you , these are thaisized , so be very careful .	但讓我先警告你們 , 這些是泰國化的 , 所以請小心點 。

and then finally , in thailand we're buddhist , we don't have a god , so instead , we say , " in rubber we trust . "	最後 , 在泰國 , 我們是佛教徒 , 我們沒有神 , 反之 , 我們說: 「 在橡膠 , 我們信任它 。 」
so you can see that we added everything to our endeavor to make life better for the people .	所以你可以看到我們把每樣東西都加入我們的努力去讓人們的生活更加美好
we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們把保險套放在旅館的冰箱和學校 , 因為酒精很容易影響判斷力 。
and then what happened ?	然後發生了什麼事 ?
after all this time , everybody joined in .	在這段時間之後 , 每個人都加入了
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國愛滋病的統計 , 愛滋病的新案例減少了90% , 根據世界銀行的統計 , 770萬人的生命因而獲救 。
otherwise there wouldn't be many thais walking around today .	否則今天不會有多少泰國人到處走動
so it just showed you , you could do something about it .	它只是顯示出 , 你可以對它做些什麼 。
90 percent of the funding came from thailand .	有90%的資金來自泰國 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助人民脫離貧窮 , 現在愛滋病有點脫節了 , 這次不是只靠政府 , 而是和企業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧困的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 無法取得信用 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是商業社群提供的東西 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試圖把他們變成赤腳企業家 , 小生意人 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法就是透過企業
so , that was done .	所以 , 那是完成的 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	這筆錢從公司投入資金到村子透過 「 樹木移植 」
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植了樹木 , 其金錢用在他們的小額貸款基金中 , 我們稱之為 「 鄉村發展銀行 」 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都會加入 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去了 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在能借到錢之前 , 你需要受過訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮之中的人 , 信用能力就必須要成為人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用能力必須要成為人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠無法擺脫貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	接著 , 在取得貸款之前 , 你必須要接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	下面我們稱之為赤腳企管碩士 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 如此一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 就會成功運用這個生意 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些生意:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹木、水果 , 還有這個非常有意思的nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 ; 這是由nike贊助的村莊 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們應該停止做鞋子和衣服 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	做這些更好 , 因為我們負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	然後我們有泰國絲綢 。
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們正在製造蘇格蘭方格紋 , 就如你們左邊所看到的 , 賣給所有蘇格蘭祖先們 。
so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	所以 , 坐在裡面看電視的人 , 請和我聯絡 。
and then this is our answer to starbucks in thailand " coffee and condoms . "	然後這是我們給泰國星巴克的回答-- " 咖啡與保險套 "
see , starbucks you awake , we keep you awake and alive .	星巴克你醒過來 , 我們讓你清醒又活著 。
can you imagine , at every starbucks that you can also get condoms ?	你能想像 , 在每一家星巴克裡你都能拿到保險套嗎 ?
you can order your condoms with your with your cappuccino .	你可以用卡布奇諾訂購保險套 。
and then now , finally in education , we want to change the school as being underutilized into a place where it's a lifelong learning center for everyone .	現在 , 最後 , 在教育上 , 我們想要改變學校 , 把學校當成沒被充分利用的地方 , 讓它成為每個人一生的學習中心 。
we call this our schoolbased integrated rural development .	我們稱之為 「 以學校為基礎的農村綜合發展 」 。
and it's a center , a focal point for economic and social development .	它是一個中心 , 一個經濟和社會發展的焦點 。
redo the school , make it serve the community needs .	重新改造學校 , 讓它滿足社區需求 。
and here is a bamboo building all of them are bamboo .	這是一棟竹子建築 , 全部都是竹子 。
this is a geodesic dome made of bamboo .	這是竹子做的地形圓頂 。
and i'm sure buckminster fuller would be very , very proud to see a bamboo geodesic dome .	我相信巴克敏斯特•富勒一定會非常非常驕傲能夠看到竹子的地形圓頂 。
and we use vegetables around the school ground , so they raise their own vegetables .	而我們在學校四周使用蔬菜所以他們可以自己種菜
and then , finally , i firmly believe , if we want the mdgs to work the millennium development goals we need to add family planning to it .	最後 , 我堅信 , 如果我們希望mdgs成功達到千禧年發展目標 , 我們就需要加上節育計畫 。
of course , child mortality first and then family planning everyone needs family planning service it's underutilized .	當然 , 先是兒童死亡率 , 然後是家庭規劃 , 每個人都需要節育計畫 , 這是不被充分利用的 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機也許感覺像是朋友 , 但真正的朋友 , 會偶爾給你微笑一下 。 在ted2013年 , 凱勒.瑞納多德摩斯 , 智慧型手機的迷你機器人可以和你一起步行 , 為你滑行一杯咖啡 , 通過桌子 , 為你做出可編程表達的反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	凱勒.瑞諾多:一個迷你機器人 , 用你的手機驅動它 。

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們romotive公司想解決的問題我和其他20位宅男都很著迷於解答
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的很想打造一個任何人都可以用的機器人不管你是八歲還是八十歲
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你得要做出一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 它不僅是真正負擔得起的 , 它還必須是人們真的想要帶回家並在孩子周圍擁有的東西 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能很詭異或不討喜 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該是友善又可愛的
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo這個機器人 , 是一個你已經知道且喜歡你的iphone的機器人 , 用來當作它的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量我們可以創造一個連接wi-fi無線網路的機器人同時擁有電腦視覺能力 , 只要150美元 , 這大約是過去這類機器人花費的百分之一 。

so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他實際上正在裝置上使用攝影機來跟蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我蹲下 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很謹慎 , 所以他會一直盯著我看 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我從這邊過來 , 他會轉向跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我走到這邊他很聰明
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他就會像其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以在很多方面 , romo像是一隻有自己想法的寵物

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上是在任意兩個智慧型設備之間做雙向的音訊和影片 。

so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以 , 我們剛剛談到遠端臨場感 , 這是很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	舉例來說 , 你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 她有iphone , 她媽媽買給她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 發送一封電子郵件給住在國家另一端的奶奶 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 。 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她一年可能只能見到她孫女一兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我最後想談談我們未來在努力的事情 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這實際上是我們的一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末就建好了 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google一個叫做blockly的開放框架上的 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖拉這些代表性語言的區塊 , 為這個機器人創造任何你想要的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何寫程式來創造romo的行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	實際上你可以在瀏覽器中去模擬這種行為 , 也就是你在左邊看到romo正在做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人 , 在現實生活中去執行它 , 在現實生活中執行該程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	接著 , 如果你有什麼值得讓你驕傲的你可以和世界上每一位擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些wifi無線網路的機器人 , 其實會互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們極度專注於建造一個大家都能訓練的機器人的原因 , 是因為我們認為 , 在個人機器人中 , 最能引人注目的使用方式 , 是針對個人機器人 。
they change from person to person .	人與人之間的改變
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	因此我們認為 , 如果你要在你家中有個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你自己想像出來的具體實現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我根本不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們知道的是 , 這不是10年或100億美金 , 也不是一個大型的類人型機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來就發生在現在 , 它將依賴小型、敏捷靈活的機器人 , 如romo , 以及像你們這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們迫不及待地想讓你們所有機器人 , 我們迫不及待地想看看你們製造出了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和社會活動家伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育子女、講故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德講述激情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常感謝 。 能來到這裡 , 非常可怕 , 是最聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡要告訴大家幾個充滿熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有句猶太諺語說我熱愛
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比事實更真誠的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想傳達一個比事實更真誠的東西 , 關於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都感興趣 , 有些甚至令我困惑 , 直到最後我把它們寫下來 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治及社會議題 , 自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我注意到我們身邊的神秘 , 所以我寫下巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了一些書 , 但是我過著匿名的生活 , 直到2006年2月 , 當我在義大利舉行奧運時 ,
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	那就讓我成了名人 。 現在在梅西百貨公司人們認得我 , 而我的孫子們認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	請允許我講一下我的四分鐘名聲
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名籌辦奧運開幕式的籌辦人打電話給我說我被選為護旗者之一
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這一定是認錯人了因為我根本不是運動員 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定可走得完體育場一圈就沒有助行器
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是開玩笑
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這會是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	5位女性將分別代表5大洲另外還有3位奧運金牌得主
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說過一套制服 , 要求我量測 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我在一個蓬鬆的大動脈裡對自己有了遠見 , 看起來像一個米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了2月中旬 , 我到了杜林 , 群眾很熱心的在街上 , 參加奧運的80支隊伍 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了一切去比賽 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但還是有運氣的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	雪上的小東西 , 冰層的一英吋 , 風的力量 , 可以判斷種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 除了訓練或運氣之外 , 最重要的是心 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都與熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報 , 宣布奧運標語 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 。 不是一直都是這樣嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們並決定我們的命運的因素 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要 「 獨行俠 」 、 「 異議者 」 、 「 冒險者 」 、 「 局外人 」 , 以及 「 叛逆者 」 , 他們會問問題、打破規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 ,
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人不會做出有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會是好前夫
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我見到其他護旗手:三個運動員 , 演員蘇珊薩蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有 , 兩位心中充滿熱情的女性來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主旺加里•馬塔伊她種了三千萬棵樹 , 藉由這麼做 , 她改變了土壤和天氣在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村莊的經濟狀況
