when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲時 , 祖父將她賣到妓院
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴這些人相信跟年紀很小的處女做愛可以治好愛滋病
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	還有那些逼孩子們每天接客515次的妓院如果孩子反抗 , 就會被電擊折磨
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我收到制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的衣服 , 但它跟我預期的米其林人裝很遠 。 其實不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但是 , 大部份的旗手也一樣 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 普遍的美麗與熱情的象徵也一樣 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、懶惰、很高、有很深的棕色 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你怎麼能有深色的皮膚而且沒有皺紋呢 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	在電視訪問中問到: 「 她怎麼看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 , 我的背總是直的 , 我也不會發出老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 你們有來自地球上最美麗的女性之一的免費建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不作聲響 , 不做咳嗽 , 不跟自己說話 , 不放屁 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有說真的那麼做 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在大約午夜的時候 , 我們被送到體育場的翅膀上 , 擴音機傳來了奧林匹克旗幟 , 開始的音樂也從這裡開始 , 阿依達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一英呎 , 不算有頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿將旗子的一角舉在肩上 。 我則在後面小跑步追還在手上握著旗子所以我的頭其實是在那面該死的旗子底下
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的鏡頭當然是蘇菲雅
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說很幸運 , 因為大部分刊出的照片 , 雖然常是出現在蘇菲雅的雙腳之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都很想去的地方
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘就是那些在奧運會場的人
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我先生聽到我這樣說時很冒犯 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們私下做的事通常不到4分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自動手做 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我還有那4分鐘不可思議的剪輯 , 因為我不想忘記老年時我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我希望永遠將奧運的關鍵字放在心中
so here's a tale of passion .	所以 , 一個充滿熱情的故事:
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 該地方是剛果境內的圖西族難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上80%的難民和被迫遷移的人都是婦女和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的死亡集中營 , 因為沒有被殺的人 , 會死於疾病或餓死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是個年輕女性蘿絲•瑪班多和她的孩子們
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 是個寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她眼睜睜看著自己的丈夫被凌虐到死 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她竟然讓她7個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子割斷臍帶然後用頭髮把斷口綁起來
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地指揮官的名字為雙胞胎命名以取得他們的青睞 , 用黑茶餵食他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法支撐他們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當軍人闖進她的牢房要強暴她大女兒時 , 她抓著她不放手就算頭上抵著槍 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 這家人存活了16個月然後 , 靠著非凡的運氣和一名年輕男子薩夏•查諾夫的熱情使她能夠進入美國救援機蘿絲•瑪班多和她的九個孩子最後到達亞利桑納州鳳凰城在那裡生活與成長茁壯
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多在斯瓦希里語中代表偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角都是堅強且富熱情的女性 , 如蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不是編造它們的 , 不需要它們 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都可見到 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在和女性及女性合作 。
i know them well .	我對他們很熟 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 臨終前 , 一個父系天主教徒和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪我五歲就已經是個熱血沸騰的女權主義者雖然當時我還沒講到智利所以沒人知道我到底哪裡出了問題
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 要為我的自由付出很高的代價 , 且是要質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能夠付出代價 , 因為每次我收到的一擊 , 我都能提供兩支 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我女兒寶拉二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會的 , 我應該繼續下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場記憶深刻的戰鬥 。 女權主義是約會對象嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於我女兒和在座各位這樣幸福的女性來說 , 是的 , 但對世界上大多數的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被逼著過早結婚、賣淫、被迫勞動 , 她們有不想要或無法餵養的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或人生 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	被強暴、毆打 , 有時還因受罰被殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對大多數今天的西方年輕女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權從來就不吸引人 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我也因缺乏男子氣概而受苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權還沒死 , 絕非如此 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 為了女神的緣故 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	改叫愛芙若蒂、維納斯或布本 , 隨便你怎麼叫 , 名字並不重要 , 只要我們了解它的內容 , 並支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	所以 , 這是另一個熱情的故事 , 這是個悲傷的例子 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	那個地方是孟加拉的一個小婦女診所
the year is 2005 .	這一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是個年輕的美國潔牙師她到診所當義工3周假期
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備乾淨牙齒了 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現那裡沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是個充滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一排女人已經等了好幾個小時可以接受治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人痛苦難當因為她好幾顆臼齒都爛了
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮知道唯一的辦法就是拔掉壞牙
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 也從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她很冒險也很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是她帶來了一些象牙 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢又熱情的心
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她喃喃祈禱 , 然後開始拔牙 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人親吻了她的手
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天衛生人員拔掉更多的牙齒
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次到達所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人跟丈夫在等她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	那女人的臉看起來像西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫到看不見眼睛
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫氣憤 , 威脅要殺掉美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮被自己所做的事嚇壞了 , 但接著 , 翻譯解釋說病人的狀況跟手術沒有任何關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫因為她趕不及回家為他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬女性過著這樣的生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最窮的人
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	縱使女性分擔世界上三分之二的勞力工作卻擁有不到1%的全球資產
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	同一份工作的薪水低於男性 , 如果他們的薪水完全沒有 , 且他們仍然是脆弱的 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 且不斷受到開發、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是提供女性教育、工作掌控自己收入的能力、繼承並擁有財產 , 對社會有益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人有力量 , 她的孩子和家人就會過得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落也會繁榮 , 最終整個國家也會如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的村落
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她跟婦女說話 , 解釋土地已經貧瘠 , 因為他們已經砍伐和賣掉了 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女人們種植新的樹一滴接著一滴
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在僅僅5或6年時間內 , 他們就擁有一片森林 , 土壤富含土壤 , 拯救了村落 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮與最落後的社會總是把女性放下
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而這顯而易見的事實卻被政府忽略 , 同時被慈善機構忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	女性相關計畫每得到1美元就有20美元用來資助男性相關計畫
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類人口的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予她們力量將改變一切不僅是科技、設計和娛樂
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以保證 , 要是女性合作連結、有知識並受教育就能為這個病入膏候的星球帶來和平與繁榮
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天的任何戰爭中 , 死傷最多的都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女與兒童 。 他們是附帶傷害的 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人掌管世界 , 看看我們所擁有的一團糟 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要怎樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是大多數人都在問的基本問題
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們要一個保存生命的世界一個生活品質是為每一個人充實不只為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在一月的時候我看到費南多•巴特羅的畫展在博克萊大學圖書館
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有任何博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊外 , 搬運巴特羅的作品 , 膽敢展示這幅畫 , 因為主題是阿布格雷布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	這些畫作都是虐待和權力暴力的大幅畫作 , 以大量的巴特羅風格呈現 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的腦中或我的心中得到那些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是無能的權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力還有濫用權力的權力
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 逼迫其他成員接受現實 , 遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則常常在改變 , 但總有益處 , 在這種情況下 , 沒用的 「 下滲效應 」 , 在經濟上行不通的 , 效果相當好 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	把濫用手法從梯子的頂端延伸到最底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女性和孩童 , 特別是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最一無所有的男人也有人可以對女人或小孩施虐
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數幾個通過性別、收入、種族和階級的權力 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為現在時機已經成熟 , 可以從根本改變我們的文明 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 若要真正改變 , 我們就需要女性化的能量 , 管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要讓女性在有權力的位置 , 且我們需要培養男性心中的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是年輕男性 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙是沒希望的 ; 我們得要等他們消失 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	沒錯 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和著名的胸部
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若有選擇 , 我寧願有顆勇士心 , 像旺加里•馬塔伊、蘇曼麗•媽媽、珍妮 , 以及蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是為了讓它更好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看四周-這些知識、活力、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們擺脫慌亂 , 捲起袖子 , 熱情地工作 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在一個和倫敦一樣大的城市中 , 共有三千萬份餐點被供應 。 但是所有的食物從哪裡來 ? 建築師卡林鋼鐵討論餵飽城市的每日奇蹟 , 並展現古代食物路線如何塑造現代社會 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolynteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市
how do you feed a city ?	如何餵飽一座城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個大問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為如果我們走進一家商店或餐廳 , 或一小時之內進到劇院大廳 , 那裡就有食物等著我們 , 神奇的從某處趕來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到倫敦這個大小的城市 , 每天就要有足夠的食物被製造、運送、買、賣、煮、吃、處置 , 類似的現象也必須發生在每天發生在地球上的每一個城市 , 都要有很了不起的效果 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這樣的地方 , 彷彿牠們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘記了這點 , 因為我們是動物 , 我們需要進食 , 實際上我們和古老的祖先一樣依賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們愈來愈多進入城市 , 更多那種大自然的景色被轉化成像我身後的景色──這是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 目的是為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些景觀很特別 , 但少有人見識過 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	而且越來越多的這些景觀並不只是用來餵飽我們而已
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們愈來愈多人搬到城市裡 , 更多人開始吃肉 , 這樣全球每年的穀物中 , 有三分之一都被拿來餵食動物 , 而不是給我們人類 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	這需要三倍的穀物事實上是十倍的穀物如果用在動物身上的話這是一個沒什麼效率的方式來餵飽人類
and it's an escalating problem too .	同樣地 , 問題也越來越嚴重 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	估計到了2050年 , 我們有兩倍的人住在城市 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	估計肉類和乳製品的消耗量將會變成兩倍 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以肉類和城市化的興起 ,
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	要餵飽六十億個肉食性動物到了2050年
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 而且如果我們繼續這樣下去 , 那將是一個我們很不可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失 , 創造出新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	儘管同時我們也失去相當於現存的可耕耕方式以獲取和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對化石燃料也非常渴望
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	西方國家每一卡路里的食物要耗去十卡路里的熱量
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	即使我們以極大的成本在製造出許多食物 , 我們事實上並不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	半數在美國生產的食物是被丟棄的
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要結束這一切 , 在這個漫長過程的最後 , 我們甚至沒有管理適當的餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	有十億人過胖 , 卻有十億人挨餓
none of it makes very much sense .	一點都不合理
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	想想看全球百分之八十的食物交易只由五間跨國企業所掌控這是個嚴峻的圖片
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們逐漸進入城市 , 世界也接受了西方的飲食習慣 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們展望未來 , 那可是不穩定的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以我們怎麼會變成這樣 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們該怎麼辦 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	嗯 , 要回答稍微簡單的問題首先 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開端 , 在古老的近東地區 , 也就是所謂的新月沃土 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如同你所看到的 , 它是新月的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	而且它是肥沃的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡有兩項非凡的發明:農業和城市主義 , 發生在同一地點 , 同時發生在同一地點 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並非偶然 , 因為農業和城市是緊密結合的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們遠古祖先第一次發現的穀物 , 產出的食物來源夠大 , 且夠穩定 , 足以支撐永久定居 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看那些定居處是什麼樣子的 , 我們可以看到它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們的周圍有生產力的農地並由像烏爾的這一座大型神廟所主宰事實上這些神廟是屬於精神型的中央食物分配中心
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排農作收割收集穀物獻給諸神再把諸神沒吃的穀物獻給民眾
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你願意 , 這些城市的所有精神和實體生活都是由他們賴以維生的穀物和收成所主宰 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 這對每一個古老城市來說都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	在西元一世紀時 , 羅馬就有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以像這樣的城市如何養活自己 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就是我所謂的 「 古代食物哩程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬得以接近海域這使得它可以從非常遠的地方運送食物
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代唯一可行的方法 , 因為運輸食物在道路上是非常困難的 , 這種方式很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	而且食物很快就壞掉了
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效率地發動了對抗如笛卡絲和埃及的戰爭 , 只為了取得它們的存糧 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說這個帝國的擴張真的是一段很長的時間畫出來的軍事化的購物中心
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提一下羅馬還曾經從倫敦進口牡蠣這個事實我覺得很了不起
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬用它的食欲來塑造它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 其他事情也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	看看17世紀的倫敦地圖我們可以發現 , 穀物是從泰晤士河運入在這張地圖的下方
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	而這些路從他們引領到廉價的道路也就是主要的市場也成為穀物市場
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看其中一條街道的名字麵包街 , 你就能知道三百年前那裡發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然對魚也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是從河裡來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	比林斯門是過去倫敦有名的魚市場一直到1980年代中期都還在使用
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真的是非比尋常 , 真的 , 當你想到
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都帶著像磚頭一樣的手機到處遊走 , 有種臭味的魚在港口上跑 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是另一個關於城市食物的特徵:一旦進入城市的根源建立起來 , 它們就很少移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類產品則是另一回事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦的大部分肉品是從西北方來的從蘇格蘭及威爾斯
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它開始出現 , 來到城市西北邊 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德倫敦著名的肉市場 , 位於那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽類從東安格利亞進來到東北方
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得自己有點像氣象女子在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥類的腳跟著鳥兒進來 , 腳上有保護著帆布的小鞋子 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當它們碰到便宜的東端時就被賣掉了這就是為什麼叫做 " 家禽區 "
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任一城市的地圖在工業時代前就建出來了你可以追蹤食物的來源
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你真的可以看到它是如何被食物實體塑造的 , 無論是讀到街道的名字 , 這給了你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前是你在星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但同時你也要想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是買賣食物唯一的場所
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面你會發現居住在這樣一個城市裡很不容易忽略你的食物來源
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃禮拜天的午餐 , 可能性是三天前在你的窗外摩擦或在外面流血 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	所以這顯然是一個有機的城市 , 是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	10年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的圖像
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	你可以看到 , 最早的火車旅客中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以 , 突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	牠們在眼不見心為淨的情況下被屠宰在鄉下的某處
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並且藉由鐵路運進城市 ,
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	一開始 , 讓它有史以來第一次能在任何地方 , 發展出真正的大小和形狀 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去 , 城市受限於地理條件 ; 過去 , 它們得要透過非常困難的實體方式來取得它們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理學中被有效地解放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	各位可以從倫敦的地圖上看到 , 在火車出現的90年後 , 倫敦從一個很容易餵飽的小點 , 一路上動物走進來的小點 , 一路走來 , 一路走來 , 很難餵飽任何人 , 無論是動物 , 還是人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然那只是個開端 。 火車之後又來了汽車 , 這個標誌著這個過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市最終的解放徹底地從自然的任何明顯關係中解放 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這種城市就沒有味道、一團亂、一團亂、一團糟 , 沒有人會想過這樣走路 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了取得食物所做的是他們上車 , 開車到郊區的某個箱子裡 , 拿著一星期的購物回來 , 想著要拿這東西怎麼辦 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	在這個時刻 , 我們與食物及城市的關係 , 徹底改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡我們有曾經是市中心的食物 , 也是城市中核心的社會核心 , 位於邊緣區域 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	過去是社會事件 , 買賣和賣食物
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們曾要料理食物 , 現在只需要加水 , 或是加一點蛋 , 如果你要做蛋糕的話 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們聞不到食物可吃的氣味
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只需讀包裝背後的標籤
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 , 也不信任它
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是珍視它 , 而是丟掉它 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統最諷刺的一點就是他們把他們所承諾的事變成更容易做得更好 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉著它能夠在任何地方、任何地方建造城市 , 其實它們讓我們遠離了最重要的關係 , 也就是我們與大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且它們也讓我們依賴那些只能傳送的系統 , 如我們所見 , 無法永續經營的系統 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們該怎麼辦呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯•摩爾就在問他自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他著作《烏托邦》這本書的首頁
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	它是一系列的半自給自足的城邦 , 聽起來有點熟悉 , 每天從彼此那兒走來 , 人人基本上都是農田 , 在後花園種植蔬菜 , 一起吃一頓共用餐 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張 , 食物是烏托邦的根本原則 , 儘管更像是未曾如此形容它 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個著名的烏托邦遠景 , 那個ebenezerhoard的 " 花園城市 " 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 一小塊大都市裡都有可耕地 , 一路連接另一塊 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說是他願景的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	甚至建造了 , 但和默斯克韋茲的這個願景沒有關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦理念的問題 , 它們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯.摩爾刻意用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它有希臘語裡的雙重含義 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以是好地、好地的意思 , 或是沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個理想的、想像的 , 我們無法擁有
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 做為一種概念性的工具 , 用來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了另一種辦法 , 像是希托邦 , 從古希臘文 「 希托 」 , 代表食物 , 「 阿波斯 」 , 也有地方可以用 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在 " 希托邦 "
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們了解到這一點 , 我們就可以把食物當作是非常強大的工具──一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 用不同的方式塑造這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果要這麼做 , 希托邦可能會長得怎樣 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	我覺得它看起來有點像
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 , 只是狗臉上的表情
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	無論如何 , 這是生活的中心食物 , 家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們為此花時間 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這是食物在我們社會的位置 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你無法擁有這樣的場景 , 除非你有像這樣的人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便說一下 , 這些也可以是男性 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	就是那些會想到食物的人 , 他們會預先思考 , 作計劃 , 他們會盯著一堆生菜 , 實際認出這些菜 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網絡的一份子
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為沒有了這一類的人 , 我們就無法擁有這樣的地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	在這裡 , 我刻意選擇這個 , 因為這個人買蔬菜
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但是網絡 , 食物是當地生長的市場 ,
it's common . it's fresh .	很普遍、很新鮮 ,
it's part of the social life of the city .	成為這個城市社交生活的一部分
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有了這些 , 就不可能有這種地方 , 本地種植的食物也是風景的一部分 , 不僅僅是這個不為人知的天然資源 。
cows with a view .	牛群帶有一種看法 。
steaming piles of humus .	用蒸汽堆積而成的香水
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	基本上這就是把整個過程結合起來 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近到多倫多做的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	那是溫室 , 孩子們會被告知所有有關食物和種植自己食物的一切 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有個叫凱文的植物 , 或許它是屬於凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	但總之 , 這類計畫在試圖將我們和大自然再度連結是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦 , 對我來說 , 是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到希托邦已經在小口袋裡存在 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	秘訣是要把它們結合起來 , 以食物作為一種看待的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這麼做 , 我們將會停止將城市視為大型、沒有生產力的區塊 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 把它們看成是有機架構的一部分 , 無可避免地連接在一起 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	但 , 當然 , 那也不是個很棒的照片 , 因為我們得要再也不用做這樣的食物了 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要多想想永續栽培 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張圖替我概括了我們應該做的思考 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	重新思考食物如何塑造我們的生活
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的影像是650年前拍的 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	是安布羅吉歐.羅倫澤提的 " 良好政府的寓言 "
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	和城市和鄉間的關係
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這件事情的訊息非常清楚
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市細心照顧國家 , 國家會照顧城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	現在 , 我想問的是 , 安布洛吉歐•羅倫澤提會怎麼畫 ? 如果他今天畫這張圖 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府的寓言會是什麼樣子的 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃什麼
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解 , 世界是我們所吃下的 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們用這個想法 , 我們可以用食物當作一種非常強大的工具 , 來改善世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	《慈悲憲章》的幾個星期後 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯研究了宗教在21世紀扮演的角色:它的教條會讓我們分裂嗎 ? 還是它會讓我們團結在一起是因為共同的利益 ? 她會檢視推動世界信仰的催化劑來重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal9、暴力、
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重新訂定黃金法則
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來我一直感到沮喪 , 因為 , 身為宗教歷史學家 , 我漸漸意識到在所有主要世界信仰中 , 慈悲的核心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	他們每一個人都演化出他們自己的 「 黃金法則 」 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時 , 它會出現在一個正面的版本中 , 「 把別人當作你自己來對待 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 " 己所不欲 , 勿施於人 "
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心臟 , 發現是什麼讓你感到痛苦 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去讓那痛苦蔓延到其他人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調的是同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它很好聽 , 而是因為它很有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則就像孔子所說的 , 「 不分晝夜 」 這個問題不只是做善事之後 , 又回到貪婪、自私的生活中 。 但是 , 為了不分日復一日地實行 , 你剝奪了自己從你的世界的中心點 , 換到另一個 , 然後你超越了自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	這會帶你進入所謂的 「 神 」 、 「 涅盤 」 、 「 完人 」 、 「 道 」 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	某種超越我們所知的東西 , 超越了我們所知的自我存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道很多時候 , 這對宗教生活是如此重要 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖會團結在一起 , 他們在爭論著深奧的教義 , 或說是仇恨的議會 , 或煽動反對同性戀或類似的事情 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	往往人們不太願意憐憫
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在跟一群宗教人士交談時 , 看到他們有著突顯的表達方式 , 正因為人們通常會希望自己是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的對象 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	那我為什麼對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們溫和地帶領我離開我的書線研究 , 帶我進入21世紀 , 讓我能對比我想像中更廣大的觀眾說話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我感到這事急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不想辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 這樣我們對待所有的人 , 不論他們在哪裡 , 就好像他們和我們一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有可行的世界要交給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 這個時代的一個偉大任務 , 就是建立一個全球化的社會 , 如同我說過的 , 讓人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教卻被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種同理心的想像行為 , 讓你自己置身於另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 在我看來
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續宣揚或強調自己的信仰 , 或是我們不寬容的一面 , 或是回到拉比山 , 耶穌那個當代 , 被一個異教徒所要求他在單腳站立時 , 總結整個猶太教義 , 他說: 「 你不願為你的鄰居做同樣的事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉和其他的東西只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教會的早期父親拉比及早期父親都說 , 任何對經文的解讀只要培養出仇恨和輕視 , 都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們必須復興這樣的精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只是因為愛的精神喚醒我們而發生 ,
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這個理想實現 , 我們可以通過ted介紹的現代溝通 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經為我們所有伴侶的回應感到極大開心 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一組人要用 「 憲章 」 來療癒近期在新加坡社會出現的分歧 , 議會的某些成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 即將有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家會帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 讓他們知道 , 同情心也在所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社群舉辦了活動和討論 , 討論以慈悲為中心的議題 , 在伊斯蘭和所有信仰中都有 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就這樣停住 。 它不能就這樣停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教誨 , 這就是我們大錯特錯的地方 , 只聚焦於相信深奧的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教誨應該要付諸行動
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	而我打算在這起我死去的日子裡努力
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想要繼續和我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 去教育並刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育是因為我們已經放棄了同情心 ,
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們經常認為這只代表對某人感到遺憾
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但是 , 如果你只是這樣想 , 你當然不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須去做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們參與媒體的目的 , 是因為媒體在幫忙消除一些我們對別人的刻板印象 , 這些意見分歧了我們彼此 。
the same applies to educators .	教育工作者也同樣適用
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望青年能夠感受到動力 , 動力和挑戰一種以同情的生活方式 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	並且也看到它要求急性智能 , 而不僅僅是一種愚蠢的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想請求學者們以他們自己和他人的傳統探討同情心的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 要鼓勵無情說話的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為有《慈悲憲章》 , 不論他們的信仰為何 , 他們都覺得有力量可以挑戰那些不被熱情的言論 , 那些鄙視的言論 , 那些來自他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 那些來自產業界的頂尖領導者 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過把憲章放到網路上
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還困在舊世界裡 , 有一大群人坐在房間裡 , 發表又一條神秘的聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	而ted為我提供了一種全新的方式來思考和發表構想 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這正是ted美妙的地方 。
in this room , all this expertise , if we joined it all together , we could change the world .	在這個房間裡 , 所有這些專業知識如果我們一起加入我們就可以改變這個世界
and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然有時 , 問題似乎也讓人覺得不舒服 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但是我想引用一段話做結尾參考英國作家牛津的作者我不常引用c.s.路易斯
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一句話一直在我腦海中揮之不去 , 打從我還是個學童時期開始 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的《四種愛》書中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他區分了愛欲的愛情當兩個人凝視對方的眼神時 , 一字不差
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這種感情與友情比較 , 當兩個人並肩站在一起 , 眼睛朝著共同的目標前進 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 ,
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我非常強烈地感受到 , 在我們維多的小小意圖中 , 當不同說服的人們團結在一起 , 肩並肩努力朝著共同目標努力 , 差異就會消失 。
and we learn amity .	我們會學習到 , 雄心壯志 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學著一起生活 , 學著認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
david macaulay relives the winding and sometimes surreal journey toward the completion of rome antics , his illustrated homage to the historic city .	davidmacaulay重獲勝有時甚至超現實的旅程 , 朝著羅馬主義者完成的羅馬防風 , 展現他對歷史城市的致敬 。
macarthur grant , art , arts , book , cities , communication , culture , design , entertainment , humor , storytelling	macarthurgant , 藝術 , 藝術 , 書籍 , 城市 , 文化 , 設計 , 娛樂 , 幽默 , 說故事 。
i draw to better understand things .	我畫畫是為了更好的了解事物
sometimes i make a lot of drawings and i still don't understand what it is i'm drawing .	有時候我畫了很多卻還是不明白我在畫什麼
those of you who are comfortable with digital stuff and even smug about that relationship might be amused to know that the guy who is best known for " the way things work , " while preparing for part of a panel for called understanding , spent two days trying to get his laptop to communicate with his new cd burner .	對於那些以數位化內容而自在的人 , 甚至是走私關係的人 , 可能會覺得有趣 , 知道最熟悉 「 事物運作的方式 」 的那個人 , 還要為 「 理解 」 做準備 , 花兩天的時間 , 試著讓他的筆電和他的新cd燒錄器溝通 。

i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我總是管理著自己的延伸 , 以至於我從來沒有想過要看指示 , 但我終於找到解答了 , 因為接到邀請時 , 最嚇人的提醒是 , 這裡沒有投影機 , 所以把這些屍體帶過來就不再有必要 , 但有些溝通的形式 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我熟知的東西 , 會特別適合在場的許多技術性思維的人 , 或是我可以談談我真正關心的事情 。
i decided to go with the latter .	我決定和後者
i'm going to talk about rome .	我要談談羅馬 。
now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	現在 , 為什麼我特別關心羅馬 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	嗯 , 我在羅德島設計學院念建築的時候是在六零年代後期
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 在我當學生的最後一年 , 也就是第五年 , 在羅馬度過 。 這改變了我的人生 。

i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了六零年代 。 我讀過它們 ; 我了解它們十分有趣 。 我錯過了它們 , 但我在羅馬度過了極為精彩的一年 , 而這是個離我心頭很遠的地方 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 只要有機會 , 我就會試著去做一些事 , 或為它做些什麼 。

all different materials , all different styles , all different times , drawings from sketchbooks looking at the details of rome .	各種不同的材料、不同的風格、不同的時間 , 從素描本圖書上找尋羅馬的細節 。

the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大部份建築物的黏土牆面覆蓋著傷痕 ; 幾世紀以來的傷疤一直在改變 , 因為這些結構已經適應下來 , 而非被拆掉 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你把它展開 , 你就會看到它背後的意思──我是說疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製造出更小的窗戶是必要的 , 因為壞人來了 , 諸如此類的 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應都被埋在了粘核之下
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以從這個palazzo的頁面剝開來展示它的內部狀況 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	更重要的是 , 我還可以向你們展示在某個壯麗的建築物的角落裡 , 那些巨大的石塊 , 或用磚頭和史特科做的假石塊 , 往往是這樣 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它就變得有點像三維立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你從一條狹小的街道中帶到一條出人意料的廣場中 , 用雙扇摺疊就可以了 。 雙扇摺疊頁--如果你就像我小時候一樣 , 讀過立體書--你希望能把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭部的頁面都包在那廣場上那短暫的時間
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	而我真的沒有做什麽比做摺疊頁更複雜的了 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但後來我又想 , 也許我可以簡單一點
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	我們來看看萬神殿和前面的羅通達廣場
here's a book completely wide open .	這是一本完全開放的書 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不把書整個打開 , 如果我只把書打開九十度 , 我們就在俯視萬神殿的正面 , 我們在看廣場的上方 , 或多或少處在廣場上 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書換一個方向 , 我們就在萬神殿的正面處望廣場 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有什麼把戲--只是一本沒有完全開放的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我想 , 也許我會在裡面做 , 甚至可以把摺疊和唯一開放的部分結合起來 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	於是我們進入了萬神廟內部 , 它會不斷地成長 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我走對路了 , 但那有點失去了人性的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想要讓大家專注在一本書上 , 一路上 , 收集資訊 , 這是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	" 鴿子的進展 " 引起我注意的是
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果那是一隻回家的鴿子那就叫做《荷馬的奧德修紀》
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是那趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個頭銜有用 , 使用它 。 但它會是一趟穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示所有我喜愛的羅馬 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	是一隻待在教堂頂上的鴿子
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天要起飛 , 做鴿子的事 。 再回來 , 整個地方都佈滿了鷹架和綠色網子 , 這只鴿子不可能飛回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以它現在是無家可歸的鴿子 , 它將必須找到另一個棲身之處 , 這讓我能夠一步一步的看進我最愛的東西 , 我們從最高的那些開始 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許牠必須回去和家人住在一起 ; 這不一定是件好事 , 但牠的確會再次將鴿子凝聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我當時想 , 這有點意思可是應該有個人也來參與一下
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想到一個老傢伙 , 他一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到任何地方去把他們弄危險 , 什麼都做 , 他們會和這個人變成朋友 , 在午餐時間中學會做些把戲 , 娛樂他之類的東西 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	在這個老人和這些鴿子之間發展出真正的鍵結
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是他病了 , 病的很重
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 也就是aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三四天沒見到他之後有一天 , 他住在一個小閣樓 , 他們把他的名字拼寫在四周 ,
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了足夠的力量 , 爬上梯子爬到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 一隻紅色的氣球 , 在那等著他 , 然後他們帶著他 , 飛過城牆 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這件事:每當他失去一隻鴿子時 , 他就會帶那隻鴿子到城牆外去 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的舊習俗中 , 死者從未被埋在牆內 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這真是個讓人愉快的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了...如果包裝行不通了 , 如果故事沒順利的話 , 我就只是想出書名 , 希望書名能引導我走向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它的確足夠讓我專注 , 我甚至會做一個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些都是書名 , 最終引領我找到了我定居下來的解決方案 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她用回教鴿的信息 , 她住在羅馬城外 , 給城市中的人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正從阿庇安公路上飛下 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看見墳墓和松果等等 , 沿途都是如此 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看見那條紅線 , 你看到鴿子的路徑 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 它變得有必要而且可能 , 試著傳達出在城市中飛越時的感受 , 卻不去真正移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔--這些你都很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒去過羅馬 , 經過大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常的現象 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大部份鴿子不會做的事:它採用了螢幕路線 , 這個裝置是我認為可以把這本書延伸到四頁以外的地方 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	於是 , 我們環繞羅馬競技場一周 , 穿過了聖母教堂 , 位在宇宙邊緣 , 和海克力士朝著河流的寺廟 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎和法蘭基羅的帕拉索•法尼斯屍體相撞 , 由米開朗基羅設計的石頭 , 建造於羅馬競技場狹窄的逃生地 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯衝到新加坡的纖維 ,
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事因為這是完全雜亂的一種完全否認觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的透視法就是只要看上去可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失點在哪 ; 有幾個就在火星上 , 另外幾位在克雷莫納 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但進入廣場 , 在和平聖母堂前面 , 在那裡 , 無時無刻都有一場足球賽在打 , 而我們卻被足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是被足球擊中的一個恐怖的畫面 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有各式各樣的片段:和平聖母堂 , 足球 , 鳥翅膀的一點點 , 什麼都沒發生 , 所以我得重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看清楚很平聖母堂--像這樣的書很靈活 , 不可思議地互動--只要把書轉過來 , 用另一種方式看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到撞擊的效果是紅色的
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後鴿子在中世紀的塔樓上空調整了過來--其中一個中世紀剩下的中世紀塔樓 , 走向聖依諾的教堂 , 周圍的圓頂向下俯瞰那廣場那廣場我們已經提過 , 已經看過和流過好幾次了 ; 這裡有剛才四條河流的伯尼座雕像 , 然後越過了美妙的聖依華堂 , 停在26英尺的天孔上 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡面到處跑 , 因為我們在飛 , 我們不用真的在這個特定的時刻擔心重力 , 所以這張圖可以在紙上以任何方式朝向 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	飛過gesu時 , 我們會有點生氣勃勃這並不奇怪用這樣的方式來模仿這個建築
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過去這面牆滿是我所提到的 " 並列 " 標誌的 " 精美雕刻 " 佈滿了我提到的 " 新月沃土 " 標誌 , 以此類推 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後我們到了palazzo的前庭也就是目的地
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓的小窗戶 , 有人在畫板上畫畫 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	牠把訊息從鳥的腿上移開 ; 牠是這麼說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	我們看著畫板 , 可以看到牠正在製作的其實是鴿子飛行的旅程的地圖 , 紅色的線穿過所有畫面 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 所以我們完成這個循環的了解 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常感謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究員 , 研究的是自我組裝的過程 , 我們不但能夠創造出能自行組合的材料 , 更像是一股dna自行組合的方式 。 它是一個在初步階段很大的概念 ; tibbit向我們展示了三項厚重項目 , 它暗示著一個自我組裝的未來會是什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天行的tibbits:我們能製造出能自己製造的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向你們展示我們製造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 不久後 , 我們的建築物和機器將會自行組裝、複製、修復它們自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要向各位展示 , 我相信是當前的製造業狀態 , 然後比較一些自然生態系統 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以 , 在當前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 五十萬至一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜 , 令人振奮的新技術 , 鋼鐵 , 水泥 , 玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人振奮的機器可以帶我們到太空--250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看一下自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈米的折疊 , 或dna有30億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統有這麼多的複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建立的複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且可以修復自己維持長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然系統有個超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以把它轉化成我們的建築環境 , 那我們建造東西的方式就會有令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以 , 如果我們想要在我們的物理環境中利用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 讓我們的建築物和機器都能辦到 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列--基本上是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以把該序列拿來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能源將允許激活 , 讓我們的部分可以折疊程序 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的糾錯冗餘 , 以保證我們已經成功地建構我們所想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	接下來我要介紹幾個項目是我在麻省理工學院的同事正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前面的兩個是巨型機器人和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目都是大規模的可重構機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們與機電設備、感應器嵌入 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你要解碼什麼便折疊成什麼 , 成序列的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 。 所以是一連串的角度 , 或輪流順序 , 你便發送這段序列通過弦 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都需要它的消息--負120它會旋轉 , 檢查它是否到了那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 參與這個項目
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想它真的能引出光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 幾千美元 , 一大堆男人為了製作這8英尺的機器人而製造 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的可以擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的可以把機器人裝到每一個部位嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 並著重被動的本質 , 或被動地嘗試重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 嘗試以實際式計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上嵌入了最根本的計算基礎元素、數位邏輯 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是一個nand邏輯閘
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個正四面體 , 就是大門會做你的電腦運算 , 你有兩個輸入的正四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是來自用戶的輸入 , 如同你在建造你的磚 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一個是從以前被放置的磚 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它會讓你在三維空間中的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	意思就是 , 使用者可以開始插入他們想要做的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它是之前做什麼 , 以及你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間裡移動--向上或向下--
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於輸出0 , 它便下降
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 它便上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這就意味著 , 我們現在的結構包含了我們所要建設的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有了所有被架構成目的的資訊 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我把它稱為自導複製 , 因為你的結構包含精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以更換零件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有局部嵌入的信息會告訴你如何解決它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	因此 , 你可以擁有攀登的東西將它讀取 , 並且可以在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有任何外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目叫做偏置鏈 , 它可能是我們現在被動自組裝系統最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它採用了可重構性和可編程性 , 讓它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一個元素鏈 ,
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都完全相同 , 且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以 , 每一條鏈 , 或每個元素 , 想要右轉或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編寫程式 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每個單位是否應該向右或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈 , 它會折疊成任何你編程的配置--在這個情況下 , 一個螺旋 , 或者這個案例 , 兩個彼此相鄰的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以編程任何立體形狀--一維 , 二維--完全被動地進入這條產業鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼關於未來的資訊 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為 , 這告訴了我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復的新可能性在我們的物理結構、建築物、機器上 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可編程 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而有了新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間的計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚其實可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的並行和分佈式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這令人興奮的潛力
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我剛才所展示的這些計畫 , 只是對這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們能實施這些新技術 , 為一個新的自組裝世界做準備 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 勘測了大陸 , 甚至還去過海底最深的地點 。 下一代還剩下什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家納森•沃爾夫斯提出了這個答案:幾乎所有一切都可行 。 然後我們開始 , 他說 , 與那些難以置信的小世界相比 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學、
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼好探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 ,
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我是去那裡榮耀一位偉大的20世紀探險家roychapmanandrews
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他當美國自然歷史博物館的期間 , andrews率領一系列到地圖上未知區域的探險活動 , 像是這裏的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個很有份量的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說他之後成為印第安納瓊斯這個角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我公開演說給一群中學學生 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡告訴各位 , 如果有甚麼事情比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人 , 那就是試著要在45分鐘的演講中 , 保持一千個12歲孩子的注意力 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在講座結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但有一個問題從那時候開始就一直困擾著我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕的女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們應該要到哪裡去探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為我們之中有很多人認為偉大的地球探索時代已經結束 , 對下一代來說 , 他們將必須去外太空或最深的海洋 , 去尋找重要的可探索事物 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有其他地方可以讓我們探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想到生物學歷史中我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未被看見的世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始發現菸草鑲嵌病的成因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是取出菸草屬植物的受感染汁液 , 透過愈來愈小的過濾器來過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他發現一定有什麼東西是比當時所知的最微小型態的生命形式還小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀人命名
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之病毒--拉丁文中的 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成地球上絕大部分的基因信息 , 比所有其他形式生命的基因信息加起來還要多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然已經有大量的實用應用和這個世界相關--像是天花的滅絕 , 預防子宮頸癌疫苗的出現 , 而我們現在知道主要是由人類乳突病毒引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現不是500年前發生的事情 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現病毒
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但是我們沒有意識到構成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界--像是深度定序 , 讓我們可以做得比只看到表面還要多 , 還能觀察特定物種的個別基因組 , 而是去看整個萬年紀 , 這些充滿了微生物的群體 , 在我們周圍 , 記錄了所有這些物種的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚以及介於其間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在常這樣做 , 來找出不清楚會造成疾病的爆發原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解一下這如何運作 , 想像我們取了你們每個人的鼻腔標本 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們平常在尋找呼吸道疾病如流行性感冒
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們首先看到的是非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會看到一些普通的可疑物--當然 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分都來自你鼻子內完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到令人非常非常驚訝的事情 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始檢視這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 在你鼻子裡大約百分之二十的基因信息 , 與我們以前見過的任何東西都不吻合 , 不論是植物、動物、菌類、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些真的在研究這種資料的小團體 , 其實我們當中有些人開始稱之為資訊生物暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何以前我們見過的東西 , 它就好像我們基因信息中沒有大陸一樣 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻腔中百分之二十的基因信息是相當多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使是在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約百分之一到二的信息是暗物質 , 無法跟我們見過的任何東西歸類或配對在一起 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們以為或許這是人工製品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定這信息是一種生命型態 , 至少一部分是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設都還在初步階段 , 但有個非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那就是埋藏在生命的基因信息中 , 是生物尚未被確認的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c、g當中 , 我們可能會發現一個全新的生命種類 , 比如beijerinck , 它會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的認知 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	那或許能讓我們找出折磨我們之癌症的原因 , 或找出我們不熟悉的爆發病症原因 , 或是在分子生物學上創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興的宣布 , 加上史丹佛、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事們 , 我們正在開始一項計畫 , 探索生物暗物質 , 以尋求新種類生命的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們沒有意識到病毒 , 組成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命型態 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚嘆說我們可能完全沒察覺到有一種新的生命存在於我們的眼前 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們也可能發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這不表示地球上沒有其它可探索的事物 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同類為下一代的探險家提供了重要的教訓像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們說出了這樣的一課 , 不要假設我們目前認為存在的就是全部的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追求任何你選擇要探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊到處都有未知的未知 , 且等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳說科學家daviddeutsch將理論物理物理學放在背後的漢堡上 , 討論更迫切的事:我們人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步是 , 他說 , 我們必須承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛deutsch在我們在宇宙中的位置 ,
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要離開肢體然後說出令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這樣做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一件事 , 事實上 , 是一段在歷史上被廣為人知的事 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 太陽系 , 環境等獨特地適合我們持續演化或創造 , 就像我們過去的想法和現在的存在一樣 。 最重要的是 , 我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有個戲劇化的名字: 「 太空船地球 」 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	在太空船之外 , 宇宙不可調和地充滿敵意 , 而其內部是我們所擁有的 , 我們所依賴的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們把太空船搞亂 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去了 。
