now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件大家都已經知道的事是與人類歷史大部分時間所相信的相反人類事實上並不是存在的中心
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	就如史蒂芬霍金說過的 , 我們只是在一個典型的星球表面的化學汙垢 , 環繞著一個典型的恆星 , 它就在一個典型的星系的最外圍 , 諸如此類 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的兩件事當中的第一件事就是說我們是在一個很不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合等等 。 第二件事 , 則是說我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是當你將這兩個真理視為深切的活著的活著真理來告訴你的人生決策 , 那麼他們似乎彼此有些衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們兩個人完全虛假 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個例子開始 。 這是個典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 我們看看四周 , 向一個隨機的方向看 , 我們看到了一面牆 , 和化學污垢 , 這些都不是典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的就是往同一個方向走幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你不會看到任何牆或化學污垢 , 你只會看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你再往遠處看 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 星星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這在宇宙中仍然不算典型 , 因為恆星存在於星系中 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	而宇宙中的大部分地方 , 一個典型的地方 , 都離任何星系都很近 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	所以 , 再進一步 , 直到我們在銀河系外 , 再往回看 , 沒錯 , 巨大的星系有螺旋形的手臂 , 擺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	在這個時點 , 我們從這裡算出了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們離宇宙中一個典型的地方還很近 ,
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達典型的地方 , 一定要先到達星系間空間一千倍的地方 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子呢 ? 典型 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方看起來是什麼樣子的 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	以巨大的開銷來說 , ted已將高清晰的跨銀河空間呈現為從星系間空間來看 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 這樣我們看得到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不完全完美你可以看到 , 在星系間的空間裡是完全黑暗 , 一片漆黑 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正盯著離你最近的恆星看 , 那顆恆星正被爆炸成為超新星 , 而你正直直地盯著它 , 在它接觸到你那光的那一刻 , 你還是無法看到甚至一絲閃光 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	那就是宇宙有多大、多麼暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星有多亮 , 多麼聰明 , 它會讓你在許多光年的距離中 , 石頭死亡 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間空間 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至不會看到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷 , 不到絕對零度三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它是非常空的 。 真空有著比我們目前所能創造出的最高真空密度小了一百萬倍的密度 。 這就是典型的地方從這個地方開始 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	那就是這地方是如此地不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以可以請我們把燈光調亮嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	現在我們如何得知一個離我們如此遙遠的環境 , 以及如此不同外星人 , 從我們習慣的事物中知道 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式存在--創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 這代表什麼呢 ? 看看比我們剛才看到的更遠--我是指用望遠鏡來看 , 你會看到類似恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們叫做類星體.類星體原意是指類星體.
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這表示有些類似恆星的東西 。 但不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 幾十億年前 , 及幾十億光年之外 , 星系中心的物質朝著一個超大質量黑洞塌陷.
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場對重力塌陷中的一些能量產生了導向作用.其中一些物質 , 以巨大的噴射流的形式回到外面去 , 照亮了極大的磁場.而我認為它有著萬億個太陽的光亮.
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人腦的物理學很難不像這種噴射流的物理學 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法一瞬間存活 。 當語言試圖描述那些噴射流中的狀況時 , 語言便會分崩離析 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這可能有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在零距離及數百萬年之久之後 ,
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那樣的噴射流發生得如此精確 , 以至於數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 和預測 , 和解釋 , 最重要的是有你用來描述當時正在發生的事情 , 在現實中 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個同類的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅是表面的圖像 , 雖然也包含在內 , 還有解釋性的模型 , 具體呈現相同的數學關係和因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠奇妙 , 信心和另一種結構相似會隨著時間而增加 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這樣特別的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那實體的物體 , 儘管不盡可能地彼此存在著相同的數學和因果結構 , 而且隨著時間的推移而越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們的化學污垢是不同的 。 這個化學污垢擁有普遍存在的狀態 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構精確度不斷地提高 , 包含著萬物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 是這個中心本身包含了整個物理現實的結構和因果的精髓 。 因此 , 與其它物理定律密切相關 。 物理定律允許了這一切 , 或者說這個可以發生 , 是實體世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	現在太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 來獲得這和宇宙其他地方的特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金觀點中其中一個正確面--我的意思是 , 它是對的 , 但它是錯的 。 有一點是錯的 。 有一點是錯的 。 它並不是用任何特殊的物理法則 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟的存在 。 它的作用 , 簡單來說就是我們這裡擁有的三樣東西 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是運算 , 計算需要一台電腦-這在無物質的情況下是製造一台電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	接著 , 第三點 , 較不容易體會 , 但就如同對於開放式的創造知識、解釋的必要性 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境被證據淹沒了 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	譬如說 , 牛頓的萬有引力定律在300年前進行測試
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但 , 過去幾十億年前 , 我們在地球上的每一平方公尺上都掉落下來的證據 , 之後的數十億年 , 還會繼續下去 。 其他的科學也同樣如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學中最基本的真理的證據就在我們星球上的真理 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的所在地充滿了證據 , 同時也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前題條件都達到了最低的供應 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我所說 , 那裡空無一物 , 那裡很冷 , 外面天黑 , 還是那裡 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹義的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像在星系間空間中的一個立方體 , 就跟我們的家一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體非常空 , 用的是人類的標準 。 但這仍然意味著 , 它包含了超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠建造一個自給自足的太空站 , 其中有一群科學家 , 他們致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類的 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在的科技已經遠遠超越了從星系間空間收集氫氣再將其轉化成其他元素等等 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但重點是 , 在一個可以理解的宇宙中 , 如果某物不被物理定律所禁止 , 那還有什麼可能阻礙我們去做 , 除了知道如何做以外呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能做到那我們就會自動獲得能源供應 , 因為轉變將是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 同樣的 , 對人類的感官來說那裡也是黑暗的 。 但你所要做的是拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是今天的一個設計 , 往外看去 , 你會看到跟我們從這裡看到的一樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	再加上一個更強大的望遠鏡你將可以看到恆星和行星
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將可以進行天體物理學研究 , 並瞭解物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡你可以打造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等.
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	也許最難做得科學研究是生物學實地考察 , 因為要到達最近的有生命得星球 , 要花上數億年的時間 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起richard--但我從來都不太喜歡生物學實地考察我想我們可以每隔幾億年才進行一次.
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間的確包含了開放式知識創造的所有前提條件 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙中的任何地方 , 都有可能變成跟我們一樣的中心 , 只要我們知道怎麼做就可以做到 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並不是在一個獨特的友好地點 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間空間有能力創造出一串開放式的解釋方式 , 那幾乎其他所有的環境也是 。 地球也是 。 地球也是受污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 這裡和那裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 而知識 , 非常匱乏 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個知識型的宇宙觀也許--我認為應該讓我們覺得很特殊.但也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為如果沒有那些必須生存的具體知識 , 我們就無法生存.
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只需要一個超新星在幾光年外飛離 , 我們都將死 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	martinrees最近剛寫了一本關於我們人類對於各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都錯了 , 最重要的是用大規模殺傷性武器來對抗恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有50%的機率能存活在這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚些時候會在研討會上談到
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為這個機率是正確的類別用來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我的確同意他的看法 。 我們能生存 , 我們不能生存 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否及時創造了相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險性並不是空前的 , 物種隨時會滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明也會終止 。 絕大多數的物種以及所有曾經存在過的文明都是現在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上來說 , 我們唯一的希望就是利用區分我們物種的這個特徵 。 我們的文明 , 來自其他所有領域的特殊關係--也就是我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋、新的知識的能力 , 成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 現在讓我把它用在當前的一個爭議上 , 不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來說明我所說的這種事情 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而這個爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但是我不是那種正確的物理學家 。 考慮到全球暖化 , 我只是一個外星人 。 對於岩層來說 , 理性的做法是嚴肅地看待現有的科學理論 。 而根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 無法避開災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果目前我們最好的選擇是阻止二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書 , 及其經濟活動的限制 , 以及花費成千上百億元美金或其他相關的高昂成本 , 那這已經是任何合理量測出來的災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而那些被倡導的行動 , 甚至沒有被提出來解決問題 , 只是稍微延後一點 。 所以這已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 可能已經太遲了 , 在任何人意識到這個危險之前 , 就已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	上世紀70年代的時候也許就已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將促成一個新的冰河期 , 數十億人將會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這一教訓對我來說很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有告知公眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們無法一直知道 。 當我們知道有一場即將發生的災難時 , 以及如何用比災難本身更低的成本來解決它 , 那麼就不會有太多爭論 , 真的 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 沒有任何預防原則 , 可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的立場 , 而不僅是針對問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一盎司的預防等於一磅的治癒方法但只有在我們知道預防什麼的情況下
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你曾被打到鼻子裡 , 那麼醫學的科學就不是教你如何避免拳頭打 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再尋求治療 , 只專注在預防上 , 那麼它也幾乎無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在用計劃來強行減排不計代價 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	降低溫度是值得注意的因素 , 與計劃是要在更高溫的溫度下生存的 , 不用花錢 , 效率和廉價地制定 。 某些因素的確存在 , 像是太空中一群鏡子將太陽偏離 , 並鼓勵水生生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西都是邊緣研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	它們不是人類努力面對這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒察覺到的問題 , 將問題做好的能力──不是無限期的好運──是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是生存的能力 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿起兩塊石板在上面刻著
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 "
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	如果被困在一個不好的制度下 , 國家要如何掙扎脫貧窮 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默開啟了一個大膽的想法: 「 特區市政府 」 , 「 全國聯盟 」 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的極端想法: 「 特區市 」
take a look at this picture .	看一下這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	對我們來說 , 它有一個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生正在做功課地點是在首都機場的路燈下因為他們家裡沒有電
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但是我見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	我們只選一個例子 , 綠色襯衣上的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也來給他個名字 , 尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢說尼爾森擁有手機 ,
so here is the puzzle .	這是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以擁有像手機那樣尖端的科技產品卻無法取得一百年的科技來在家裡發電
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案就是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的制度 , 可以防止雙贏辦法的產生 , 當人們可以把新科技帶進來 , 並讓像尼爾森這樣的人也能使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司遵循的制度運作 , 指出它必須用很低的補貼價格來銷售電力 , 事實上 , 這個價格低到連在賣出的每一套 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既無資源、也無動機去幫許多用戶配電
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這條規則
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他見過 , 有可能會有另一種規則 , 也就是企業能賺到一點利潤的規則 , 所以他們有誘因去簽署更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	正是尼爾森手機公司從基礎行動電話購買的那種規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經知道這些規則如何好好運作了 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變用電費的制度 , 但卻跑到一場從企業或消費者身上抗議 , 他們想保存現有補貼的比率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他深陷其中一些規則 , 阻止他讓雙贏的解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	而尼爾森也只得困在路燈下讀書
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	那時真正的挑戰是試著找出我們能如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們能制定一些規則來改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我主張 , 有一個很普遍的抽象洞見 , 就是 , 如果我們能給予人們更多選擇 , 更多的領導者更多的選擇 , 在許多國家 , 也都是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 呈現出這兩者間的反對聲浪很有用 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導者的那種選擇 , 例如給總統選擇 , 提高電價的選擇 , 奪走經濟中人民想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給其中一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多的選擇 , 那就會給我們一套規則 , 讓我們脫離陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也有網路用
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說如果你想見到規則的破壞 , 規則可以讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署拍攝的地球夜景 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大來看這裡你可以看到北韓這塊跟鄰近黑洞相比很像
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會感到驚訝 , 因為北韓的體制使人留在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是要認識到北韓和南韓開始時用的是一模一樣的規則 , 無論是法律或法規 , 還是在更深層的層面 , 理解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了一些選擇 , 導致非常多樣化的路徑 , 用於他們一組規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們能改變──我們人類能改變我們用來和彼此互動的規則 , 不論是好是壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 這裡的輪廓
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗與它的鄰居多明尼加相比 , 這裡的居民人數差不多
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相較於波多黎各 , 他們的居民數目只有海地或多明尼加共和國的一半 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則可能有壞處 , 因為政府很弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	這不僅僅是規則條例不好 , 因為政府太強勢、壓迫 , 就像北韓的情況一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想創造一個有良好體制的環境 , 我們不能僅僅撕下去而已 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須找到方法去建立
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展現出與規則合作的潛力與挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到資料圖表的一開始 , 中國是世界高科技領導人 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人的科技像煉鋼、印刷、火藥等先驅
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的制度來鼓勵這些想法的傳播 , 一個利益的動機 , 可以鼓勵散播出去 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	且他們很快就採用規則 , 來放慢創新 , 將中國從世界其他地方切斷 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以當其他國家在創新 , 以發展更新的科技 , 同時發展更新的規則 , 中國也被切斷了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入高於世界其他地方的收入都停滯不前
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	顯示了中國的平均所得佔美國平均所得的百分比
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代時你們可以看到這個數字大約是3%
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況有了改變 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國開始起飛中國人開始很快地趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到晚上去看地圖 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 一個轉變為中國體制的過程 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的這個點 , 大家可以在輪廓邊上看到 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港本來是中國領土中很小的一點在20世紀大部分的時候都是遵循一套很不一樣的規則在運作 , 與中國其他地方的主要規則在當時的市場經濟環境中被複製並由英國主導
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是數百萬人都可以去的地方 , 從大陸到始於縫紉上的工作 , 像是製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入的過程 , 增加技能 , 在那裡能夠快速成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個範本 , 像鄧小平這種領導者能夠複製 , 當他們決定把整個大陸推向市場模式 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有人立刻轉向市場模式 , 不如說 , 創造一些特區 , 可以做些什麼 , 某種意義上是英國人所做的:讓機會與市場規則一同前往 , 和那些想參與選舉的人一起工作 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍建了四個經濟特區中國人可以來這裡工作 , 都市在此迅速成長 ; 還有一些外國企業可以進來並製造東西的區域 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港旁邊的一個特區 , 有一座城市叫做深圳 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市有台灣企業 , 讓在座很多人都擁有的iphone , 他們靠著從中國人搬到深圳的勞動 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有十四個沿海城市 , 在相同的意義下 , 最終 , 在這些地方展現出成功 , 在這些地方 , 人們可以選擇進入 , 他們聚集起來 , 是因為他們提供的優勢 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡 , 成功促成了一項共識 , 使整個經濟體向市場模式邁進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了以下幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保留給人的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:運作的規模是對的 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試圖改變一個村落的規則 , 你就可以這麼做 , 但村落規模小到無法得到你能得到的益處 , 如果你有數百萬人 , 所有人都遵守好的體制 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家的規模太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試圖改變國家的規則 , 你不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看事情發展成如何 , 讓其他人開始放大嘗試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但 , 城市給你這個機會 , 來創造新地方 , 用新規則 , 讓大家可以選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們就夠大了 , 足以讓我們在數百萬人一起合作時 , 獲得所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以這個提議就是我們構思了一個叫做特區市的東西 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個明確規範的憲章開始 , 來吸引那些需要我們建設城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引那些會建立起基礎設施的投資者──電力系統、道路、港口、機場、及建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引企業他們會先請來搬移的人
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	然後你會需要吸引家家戶戶願意搬來住 , 永久居住在那裡 , 養育子女 , 為孩子接受教育 , 得到第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	隨著那個憲章 , 人們會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	這座城市可以被建造起來 。
and we can scale this model .	而我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍的
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲章中被記錄下來 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	如果我們能在無人居住的土地上 , 建造城市的可能性就已經被實現了 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	從無人居住的領域開始 ,
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以來到新的規劃下居住 , 但沒有人是被迫的 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者選擇
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們期望的領導者們的選擇我們必須允許國家之間互相合作的潛力 。 實際上 , 中國和英國的合作方式 , 首先是市場模式的奴隸 , 然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國 , 透過在香港的行動 , 不經意地減少了世界貧窮現象 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫都還要大 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們能讓這樣的合作模式再度重現我們可以使全世界都受惠
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下這會牽扯到負責任的地位 , 將控制權下放給另一個國家 , 以掌握某些特定的行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我說這句話時 , 有些人開始會想: 「 這只會讓殖民主義復活嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但很重要的是要認清當我們開始思考這些事情時會產生的那種情緒 , 能夠阻擋我們 , 讓我們退縮 , 關閉我們的能力 , 以及探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 在一些援助計畫中 , 殘留的就是它涉及了強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這種模式的重點在於選擇 , 不論是領袖 , 或將來住在這些新地方的人民 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是解藥 , 解藥是強迫和優越的 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	我們來談談如何實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們選一個特別的領袖 , raulcastro , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國做到的 , 但他在古巴並沒有一個香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他還是有一點點光線在南部 , 那兒有著很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣附近有一個地區 , 在那裡 , 條約賦予美國行政權責任 , 一塊大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大的土地 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大總理對他說: 「 聽著 , 洋基斯有個可怕的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你們加拿大何不接手呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建造一個特殊的行政區
allow a new city to be built up there .	允許一個新城市在那上面興建 。
allow many people to come in .	允許許多多人加入
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近的香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些公民也會搬進那座城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會憋住 , 但這就是那通往現代經濟和現代社會的通路 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	現在 , 這個模式還能在哪裡試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我曾和非洲的領導人談過 ,
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們當中許多人完全了解特區的想法 , 讓人們可以選擇為制度 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	是 「 改變規則 」 的制度
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種制定新規則的方式 , 不需要強迫就讓人民 「 選擇 」 , 反對 「 強制 」 可以強制執行 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下他們可以對長期投資者做出更有保障的承諾這些投資者將會建造港口 , 建設道路 , 在新城市 , 他們可以做出更有保障的承諾只要他們能與合夥的國家一起做 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	或許甚至在某些安排有點像信託管理帳戶 , 你把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡 , 合作國家要為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲有很多的土地可以用來建造新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是一張我沿著海岸飛行時照的照片
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣一大片延伸出去的土地有數億人可以居住
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 若我們總結一下 , 不只想著一、二個特區客機 , 還會有數十個城市 , 協助創造數億個城市 , 也許在未來的世紀 , 有數十億人搬到城市去 , 讓他們有足夠的土地容納他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在全世界 , 如果我們晚上看這些燈光 , 唯一會造成誤導的就是 , 看上去 , 世界上大部分的地區都已經被建立起來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把所有土地的這個代表作
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊代表地球上所有的可耕地
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被30億人居住的城市佔據了的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到這個長方形的底部你會發現這些有30億居民的城市只佔了地球上所有可耕地面積的3%
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以 , 如果我們想要為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們就會變成這樣 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們會從可耕地的3%走到4% 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大地減少人類在地球足跡上的足跡 , 做法是建造更多人類能搬到的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是依照良好的規則來管理 , 它們可以是安全的城市 , 在那些城市中 , 人們不受犯罪、疾病 , 及公共衛生不良 , 在那裡 , 有機會找到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到像電力這樣的基本公共事業
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以得到教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要打造第一座 「 特區 」 城市 , 要花什麼代價 , 才能做得更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	一本手冊會有幫助 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們能做的就是撰寫一些細節 , 可能順利進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理這些城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者們跑到野外去
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 比如 , 假設加拿大不只能用卡斯楚的方式來處理 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西也參加了 , 西班牙也參一腳 。 也許古巴想成為四向合作的一員 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有先例可循 , 但很容易就能解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要怎麼融資 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	新加坡和香港都是城市 , 為他們一開始所擁有的土地帶來了巨大的收穫 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地價值的收益來支付像警察 , 法庭費用但是學校系統和健康照護系統這使得這個地方更吸引人 , 更吸引人的生活環境這使得人們的收入增加 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更加珍貴
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 協助建設這個區域的人的動機 , 並建立起基本的規則 , 走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有許多其它的細節 , 像這樣 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓那些在第一份工作就很便宜、負擔得起的建築 , 把類似iphone的建築物組裝起來 , 讓那些建築物能更有效率 , 並確保它們是安全的 , 所以不會因為地震或是颶風而倒下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術上的細節尚待解決 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些事的人 , 已經知道沒有路上的阻礙 , 也沒有障礙 , 除了想像力失靈之外 , 那會讓我們無法實現真正的全球性雙贏解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來做總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們能過得好的原因 , 即使地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為思想的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和別人分享想法 , 當他們發現想法時 , 他們就和我們分享了 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	不像稀有物品 , 分享意味著我們每個人都會獲取更少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式來思考想法 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:規則主宰我們彼此的互動 ; 規則像是 , 讓我們來訂個稅制 , 來支持一個研究大學 , 提供一些免費的知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有個制度 , 在那裡 , 我們擁有一塊土地 , 用政府的辦公室來註冊 , 讓大家可以自行承諾去承擔抵押品 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷在我們這個制度上創新 , 尤其是想出一些改變規則的制度 , 我們就不會卡在不良的制度上 , 那麼我們就能不斷進步 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 這樣尼爾森和他的朋友就不再需要在路燈下學習了 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	克萊格•凡特從他史詩般的圓環世界遠征之後 , 對於他團隊目前所發現的數百萬基因進行了研究 , 來描繪海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特寫在dna和海上 。
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	休息時 , 有幾個人問我關於老化辯論的意見 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這會是我對它的唯一評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者非常過時的悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我在這18分鐘內要告訴你們的是我們如何從破解基因密碼轉換到開始自我編碼的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅十年前的這個月我們公佈了第一組取自一種非寄生有機體的基因序列像是嗜血桿菌
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年到4個月進行的基因組研究 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以用兩到八個小時來完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以在過去的十年中 , 大量的基因組被加進來:大部分的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類的基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十多年前這個階段的基因組學研究發現 , 到今年年底 , 我們可能已經完成了三到五組基因組的測序 。 大概是幾百組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金會獲得了資助 , 到今年為止 , 做了130組基因組的測序 , 作為環境有機體的副方案 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	因此讀取基因編碼的速度已經改變 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 我們看看 , 外面到底有什麼 , 我們幾乎不在地球上現有的東西上挖掘表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部份人都沒有意識到 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球上生物總量的一半 。 而所有的動物只佔所有生物總量的千分之一 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許是一些牛津人很常做的事 , 但如果你曾經到過海裡 , 吞一口海水 , 別忘了 , 每一毫升都有大約100萬隻細菌和一千萬隻病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 少於五千種微生物被歸類為兩種 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了索爾三世的探險活動 , 在那裡 , 進行了很棒的海洋考察 , 嘗試每200英哩進行一次採樣 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始我們的實驗計畫 , 接著搬到哈利法克斯 , 到美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫越印度洋的途中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是非常艱難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上這樣做 , 有部分原因是要讓年輕人興奮地想要進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗是非常簡單的
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只要把海水用過濾器收集不同的大小生物體 , 然後把它們的dna帶回在岩城的實驗室 , 在那裡我們可以在24小時內完成一億個字母的基因編碼的測序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這個活動 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 一般認為在我們眼中的視覺色素 , 環境中只有一兩種有機體擁有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎所有生活在海洋上方溫暖地區的物種都有相同的感光器 , 利用陽光作為牠們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬種新基因 , 和多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在將它延伸到空氣中 , 加上史隆基金會的資助 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們測量有多少病毒和細菌所有人每天都呼吸和呼吸 , 特別是在飛機上或是密閉的講堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們利用一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 僅僅一天之內我們蒐集到10億微生物的數量 , 在紐約市一棟大樓的樓頂過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們現在正處於排序的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在收集資料方面 , 就在加拉巴哥群島的位置 , 我們發現幾乎每隔200英里 , 我們就發現海洋中的樣本有著極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	這當中有些符合邏輯 , 根據不同的溫度梯度來計算 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張以溫度為基礎的衛星照片--紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色則是冷的--我們發現 , 溫水樣本和冷水樣本之間有著極大的差異 , 取決於豐富的物種 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令人訝異的事情是這些光感接收器偵測到不同波長的光線 , 我們可以根據他們的胺基酸序列來預測這現象 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	從地區到地區的這些差異極大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外 , 在深海 , 那裡大部分是藍色的 , 感光細胞傾向於看見藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化更大 , 可能向紅外線和紫外線偏向極端 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們基因庫的樣貌 , 我們整合了所有的資料 , 包括所有我們遠離探索的資料 , 這些資料代表地球上超過一半的基因資料 , 總計大約有兩千九百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放進基因家庭裡 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現了已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但是我們在環境中所採取的每個新樣本 , 都加入了這些新族群的線性樣本 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於發現基礎基因、元件和生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看所謂的進化樹圖時 , 我們在右上角與動物在同一區 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	其中大約兩千九百萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有大約兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果把所有動物的基因組合起來 , 我們所共享的基因組大概只有三萬隻以下 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我看待這些基因現在不僅僅是進化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們從基因中心論來看-或許回到了理查•道金斯的想法而不是基因組中心論 , 這是這些基因組成的不同構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 也就是合成dna的能力 , 在過去十年到二十年間 , dna序列的速度一直改變 , 變得非常快速、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對於人造基因組的第一個想法來自於1995年我們在第二組基因組的測序 。 這是從mycoplasma生殖支原體中取得的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有非常好的t恤上面說: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約五百個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800對基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只需要問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要八百種 , 另外五百種 , 有比較小的基因組 , 可能會組成一個最小的作業系統嗎 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	於是我們開始進行轉位子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是隨機插入基因編碼中的小段dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果置入基因的正中間 , 會阻斷其功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 上面有可以接受轉位子插入的基因 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現 , 環境對此是非常關鍵的 , 你只能依據環境中確實存在的本質或不可或缺的基因來定義 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也試著用更直接的智慧方法 , 和13種有機體的基因組做比較 , 我們試著比較它們所有的基因組 , 看看它們有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現了173種基因 , 只有173種 , 只有13種有機體的基因 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一個細胞內的寄生蟲 , 池子會稍微擴大一點 , 當我們觀察核心基因組的310左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以 , 我們認為我們可以擴展或收縮基因組 , 根據你的觀點來看 , 可能從最少的500到400個基因中 , 擴展到300到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一可以證明這些想法的方法是建造一條包含有這些基因的人染色體 , 我們不得不以一套套以模板為基礎的模組來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現大片碎片中合成精確的dna是極其困難的
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 是我的同事 , 研發出令人振奮的新方法能讓我們在兩週內合成出5000個鹼基對的病毒只需100%的精確度就在它的序列和生物學上
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個令人振奮的實驗我們將合成的dna注入細菌體內 , 突然間dna開始製造病毒粒子反過來殺死細菌
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是人造病毒的第一年之前就產生小兒麻痺病毒而是活躍的十分之一花了三年的時間
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構圖 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在自行製造硬體的例子 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立即跳入關心生物戰的議題上 , 我最近在參議院委員會舉行前發表了證詞 , 也參加了美國政府設立的專門委員會來檢討這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 將現實記在心中是很重要的 , 與人們的想像力相反的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經完成測序的病毒基因組都可以
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會馬上對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚恐 , 但這個生物的dna並沒有傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使製造出天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓國安部門擔憂的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	而只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯兩國付出極大努力企圖製造生物戰的媒介
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這項研究真的被終止了 , 那將來在製造設計病毒上就應該不會有足夠的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為兩年內就有可能有單細胞生物 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	而我們所擁有的這些真核細胞 , 可能在十年內就有可能實現 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以 , 我們現在正在製造數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變放入這個人造染色體的卡帶和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 要怎麼把所有其他的都放在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片段開始 , 接著我們有一個同源重組的系統將這些片段組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體得來的deinoccusradiodurans得來的它可以承受三百萬雷得的輻射而且不會被殺死
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發過後它會在12至24小時內重組自己的基因 , 在它的染色體被完全拆散後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上普遍存在 , 也許現在的外太空是因為我們在那裡的所有旅行 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是經過50萬拉德輻射照射過後的杯子 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始碎裂 , 而微生物停在底部 , 變得更開心、更開心 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際狀況的照片上面的圖片顯示的是經過一百七十萬拉德輻射後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被完全拆散 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是相同的dna在24小時後自行重組 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	這些生物能夠做到這一點 , 真的很讓人吃驚 , 我們在這個星球上有成千上萬種不同的物種可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	因此我們認為人造細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了瞭解生物學的基礎 , 同時也是希望是環保及社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們所測序的第三個生物上 , 詹氏甲烷鏈球菌──它生存在沸騰的水溫中 ; 它的能量來源是氫 , 它的碳元素則是來自環境中的二氧化碳 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 現在有數千種不同的生物 , 它們都從二氧化碳中生存 , 而能將其捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	因此 , 我們不用從石油中取得的碳 , 而是利用碳 , 從大氣層中捕捉回來 , 轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一個有機體 , 可以靠一氧化碳維生 , 我們把水分解 , 來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有許多可以改造甲烷的路徑 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦有一個大型的計畫在挪威石油採集現有的石油收集並將在那裡的甲烷轉變成有用的產品
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	不久之後 , 我認為會有一個新領域出現 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有這些新的合成功能 , 這些巨大的基因陣列和同源重組技術 , 我們想我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可以製造出也許一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 如同所有生物學 , 你可以通過篩選來獲得選擇 , 無論是用來篩選氫氣製成或是化學製成 , 還是僅限於可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	若要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 在我們能接觸到的範圍內 , 一定會很清楚 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用的過程直接從陽光產生氫氣
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧不敏感的氫化合物將會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在進行組合 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖及發酵的酵素 , 在同一個細胞中製造乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	利用微生物進行製藥生產的研究已經在主要實驗室中進行 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物化學成分比我們最好的化學家能產出的還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可能是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 也許取代了整個石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策的研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年我們延遲了實驗的開始直到我們完成了一個一年半的生物倫理審核是否應該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 ,
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這的確是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖使用他們的教義作為法律書籍 , 卻找不到任何關於禁止製造生命的條件 , 所以這方面就沒問題了 。 最終的擔憂是生物戰的方面 , 卻給了我們開始進行這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會剛剛資助了一個多機構的研究項目來探究這個項目對社會的風險和益處還有科學團隊比如我自己的團隊應該在這個領域使用的規則我們試著在未來建立好的例子
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了對生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 就我們是否能設計出能產生乾淨能源的產品 , 也許可以徹底改變發展中國家可以做到的 , 並提供各種簡單的處理 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普津巴多說 , 快樂和成功都根植在我們看不見的特質中:我們以朝向過去、現在和未來的方向前進 。 他建議 , 我們準時校準自己的觀點 , 來改善我們的生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理、科學、
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	philipzimbardo開了一間健康的開處方 , 就要準時到來
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些想法 , 關於時間的秘密力量 , 在很短的時間內 ,
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好 , 開始計時.30秒
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 。 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	重點是時間 。 結束序列 。 拿一個吧 。

philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:讓我們一起來調查亞當的誘惑校長的談話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 別那麼渴望洗澡 。 咬一口吧 。 」 「 我照做了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	" 咬一口 , 亞當.不要拋棄eve. "
" i don't know , guys .	「 各位 , 我不知道 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 咬一口 。 搞什麼鬼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生就是誘惑 。 這一切都是為了產出、抗拒 , 是的 , 此時此刻 , 衝動性、焦點、現在及未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾美德會落入當下的熱情中 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些曾宣誓要在婚前確保貞操的少女感謝小布施-大多數 , 約有60% , 會在一年內得到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	而且大多都不使用避孕措施 。
so much for promises .	非常適合做承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在來試試四歲孩童 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以擁有一顆棉花糖 。 但是如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆了 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 得付出代價 ,
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	發生的狀況是 , 三分之二的孩子會給予誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等 。 其他人 , 當然的等了 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們延遲了一下 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米舍爾 , 我斯坦福大學的同事 , 在14年後 , 試著去發現那些孩子有何不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多方面 , 反抗的孩子和產生出來的孩子之間存在著很大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒得到sat分數250分的孩子們 ,
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那很巨大 , 就像是一整組不同的iq點
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 , 他們是更好的學生
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們自信和堅決 。 而我今天的關鍵 , 你們的關鍵在於 , 他們是以未來而非當前的焦點 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是時間觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	看待時間是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你人類經驗的流動分成時間區域或時間類別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動地、不自覺地、
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平都不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏頗 , 因為你學會了過度使用它們 , 其他的基礎設備 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做的決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你做出的決定是要基於動作 ,
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人而言 , 這只與當下情況有關 , 別人做的事和你的感受有關 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們以這種形式作決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現實主義 」 , 因為他們所關注的就是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是不重要的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是關於 「 我過去經歷過的這種情況如何 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定是以過去的記憶為基礎 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 " 懷舊主義 " 因為他們關注的是過去
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人而言 , 那不是過去 , 不是現在 , 只和未來有關 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是在於預期的後果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們會稱他們為 " 未來型態 " 他們關注的重點在於將來
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想論 , 時間觀念上的悖論 , 是影響你做出的每個決定 , 你都完全沒有意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有這樣的一個偏差的時間角度 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	實際上 , 這裡有六種 。 有兩種方式可以當下存在 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以 「 懷舊 」 , 有兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你也可以稱它為 " 享樂主義 " , 也可以稱它為 " 生活的樂趣 " , 或者 " 由於 " 不論 " , 你的生活 " 都可以 " 掌控 " 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 「 未來 」 、 「 設定目標 」 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你可以是超然的未來:也就是 , 生命始於死亡 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 轉移時間觀點的流暢度 , 取決於局面的需求 , 這是你要學的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔案 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " , 適度 " 未來 " 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	和適應現狀主義的準則 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	永遠放低 " 負面懷舊 " 和 " 宿命論 "
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最佳時光的混合是你從過去得到的正面回饋給你根源 。 你連結你的家人、身份和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	未來你能得到的是一對翅膀 , 可以飛到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從 「 享樂主義 」 得到的能量 , 是自我探索的能量、地點、人、感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度的時光檢視都有更多的負面而不是正面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來為成功犧牲什麼呢 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	犧牲家庭時間 ; 犧牲朋友時間
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲快樂時光 ; 犧牲個人崇拜時光 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	犧牲業餘愛好 ; 犧牲睡眠.所以這會影響他們的健康.
and they live for work , achievement and control .	為工作、成就和控制而活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我確信這會與一些tedsters引起共鳴
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這句話引起我的共鳴 。 我成長過程中是個貧窮的孩子 , 住在南布朗克斯貧民窟 , 一個西西里島家庭 , 每個人都過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡 , 身為一個未來的前人 , 走到頂端 , 做出這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入了 , 讓我有未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等 , 你就會得到兩顆 , 直到我學會保持平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加入了 「 現狀主義 」 , 把焦點放在過時的正面 , 所以 , 在76歲 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這種方法用在世界各地的問題上:改變輟學率、增加吸毒、增加青少年健康、治好退伍軍人的創傷後壓力症候群──隨著時間隱喻──奇蹟──促進可持續性和保育 , 減少身體康復費用 , 此項目有50%的退出率 , 改變自殺式恐怖份子的訴求 , 修正家庭關係 , 修正家庭衝突的時間 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以我想在結尾再說一句:生活中的許多難題可以透過了解你的時間觀和其他人的時間觀來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 很明顯 , 但我認為後果真的很深刻 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	當今的頭條有多少在100年後會很重要呢 ? 1000年 ? 克裏克•卡通的 「 長遠新聞 」 計畫收集當今不只重要的新聞而且會在幾十年後引起共鳴在ted2010年他在ted2010年提出頭條標題這些頭條有潛力塑造我們未來
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球議題 , 媒體 , 新聞 , 科學
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在 , 真正的消息是
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞中 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單是路透社一家一年就發佈350萬則新聞
that's just one source .	那只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事長期來說 , 有多少才是真正重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長遠新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是一個由tedsters所創立的長期基金會的計劃包括kevinkelly和stewartbrand
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	而我們在找的新聞 , 可能在50或100或10 , 000年後仍然會是重要的新聞故事 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過那個過濾器來檢視新聞 , 很多事情會落在一邊 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以去年a.p.的首要故事來說 , 在十年內 , 這會影響嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還蠻酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頭條是經濟問題 , 我敢打賭 , 遲早 , 這次經濟衰退 , 會變成陳年往事 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 怎樣的故事才能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 就科學而言
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有朝一日 , 小飛行器會經過我們的血液流動 , 修理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠的話 , 那一天已經在你身邊了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真的蜜蜂毒液攻擊腫瘤 ; 他們把基因送到大腦中 ; 他們打造的機器人可以爬過人體 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源方面呢 ? 我們要如何養活90億人口 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今我們餵養六十億人是有困難的 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天所聽到的 , 這裡有超過10億人正處於飢餓狀態 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	沒有基因改造作物 , 英國人會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲在農業研究上已經賭上了十億 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會變得非常不同 , 如果中國設定議程的話 , 他們也可能做到 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們已經開始在孩子們的職業上進行dna檢測 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在尋找各種途徑 , 來回推我們已知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近有一些發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群現在已經傳播到每個大陸--但南極洲 。 有個自導的機器人科學家很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命可能不再需要我們了 , 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎有沒有人類 , 生命就會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但去年 , 我選了長久以來的新聞報導 , 上面是這則:月球上找到的水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	要想把蟻群放上去就容易多了 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某人可能會寫一份大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家carolynporco展示的圖片從卡西尼航行到土星 , 主要集中在它的最大衛星 「 泰坦 」 , 以及冷凍土衛二上 , 似乎它會噴射出冰 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署 , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 空間 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco要我們飛到土星去
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我會帶大家去旅行 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是一段旅程 , 你和我已經踏上許多年了 , 大約五十年前 , 當人類第一次離開地球時 , 這段旅程便開始了 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年中 , 我們不僅真的踏上了月球的物理起點 , 我們還把飛行器給了所有的八個行星 , 我們在小行星上著陸 , 和彗星相輔相成 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一架太空飛船正向冥王星駛去 , 之前所知的天體就是一個行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類旅程的一部分:一趟用來了解某樣事物的航行 , 去了解我們的宇宙起源 , 了解我們的起源 , 還有地球 , 我們的星球 , 以及我們賴以生存的星球 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中所有我們想去的地方 , 找到像這樣的問題的答案 , 這裡有土星 。 我們在1980年代早期造訪過土星之前就到過土星了 。 但是我們對土星的研究 , 從卡西尼號太空船開始進行了更加深入的探究 , 經過了整整七年的行星空間 , 在2004年夏天穿越土星運行軌道 , 發現了當時人類抵達的最遠距離的機械裝置 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是一個豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它帶來神秘 , 科學洞察 , 和顯然比起來 , 光彩奪目 , 這系統的研究 , 具有巨大的宇宙能力 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 單單研究光環 , 我們就能學到很多關於星星和氣體的光碟 。 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這裡有一張仙女星雲的美麗照片 , 是我們離銀河系最近 , 最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這是由哈勃太空望遠鏡拍攝的旋渦星系 , 美麗的部分 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 返回土星的旅程 , 其實是人類旅程的一部分 , 也是個比喻 , 比喻是人類旅程的一部分 , 用來了解我們周遭一切事物的相互關聯性 , 以及人類如何融入照片中 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	我很痛苦 , 我無法用卡西尼號來告訴各位我們所學過的一切 。
